	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Academic degree</h1>

</div><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>An <b>academic degree</b> is a qualification awarded to students upon successful completion of a course of study in <a href="/wiki/Higher_education" title="Higher education">higher education</a>, usually at a <a href="/wiki/College" title="College">college</a> or <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a>. These institutions commonly offer degrees at various levels, usually including <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">bachelor's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master&#39;s degree">master’s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doctorates" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctorates">doctorates</a>, often alongside other <a href="/wiki/Academic_certificate" title="Academic certificate">academic certificates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Professional_degree" title="Professional degree">professional degrees</a>. The most common <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_degree" title="Undergraduate degree">undergraduate degree</a> is the bachelor's degree, although in some countries there are lower level higher education qualifications that are also titled degrees (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Associate_degree" title="Associate degree">associate degrees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foundation_degree" title="Foundation degree">foundation degrees</a>).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Meeting_of_doctors_at_the_university_of_Paris.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Meeting_of_doctors_at_the_university_of_Paris.jpg/190px-Meeting_of_doctors_at_the_university_of_Paris.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Meeting_of_doctors_at_the_university_of_Paris.jpg/285px-Meeting_of_doctors_at_the_university_of_Paris.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Meeting_of_doctors_at_the_university_of_Paris.jpg/380px-Meeting_of_doctors_at_the_university_of_Paris.jpg 2x" data-file-width="966" data-file-height="1522" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Meeting_of_doctors_at_the_university_of_Paris.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Meeting of doctors at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Paris" title="University of Paris">University of Paris</a> (16th-century miniature)</div></div></div>
<h3><span id="Emergence_of_the_doctor.E2.80.99s_and_master.E2.80.99s_degrees_and_the_licentiate"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergence_of_the_doctor’s_and_master’s_degrees_and_the_licentiate">Emergence of the doctor’s and master’s degrees and the licentiate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Emergence of the doctor’s and master’s degrees and the licentiate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The doctorate (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>: <i>doceo</i> “I teach”) appeared in <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">medieval Europe</a> as a license to teach (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>: <i>licentia docendi</i>) at a medieval university.<sup id="cite_ref-Lexikon_des_Mittelalters:_Doctor,_doctoratus_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lexikon_des_Mittelalters:_Doctor,_doctoratus-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Its roots can be traced to the <a href="/wiki/Early_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Early church">early church</a> when the term "doctor" referred to the <a href="/wiki/Apostles" title="Apostles">Apostles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Church_fathers" class="mw-redirect" title="Church fathers">church fathers</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> authorities who taught and interpreted the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lexikon_des_Mittelalters:_Doctor,_doctoratus_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lexikon_des_Mittelalters:_Doctor,_doctoratus-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The right to grant a <i>licentia docendi</i> was originally reserved to the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_church" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic church">church</a> which required the applicant to pass a test, to take oath of allegiance and pay a fee. The <a href="/wiki/Third_Council_of_the_Lateran" title="Third Council of the Lateran">Third Council of the Lateran</a> of 1179 guaranteed the access – now largely free of charge – of all able applicants, who were, however, still tested for aptitude by the ecclesiastic scholastic.<sup id="cite_ref-Lexikon_des_Mittelalters:_Licentia_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lexikon_des_Mittelalters:_Licentia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> This right remained a bone of contention between the church authorities and the slowly emancipating universities, but was granted by the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a> to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Paris" title="University of Paris">University of Paris</a> in 1231 where it became a universal license to teach (<i>licentia ubique docendi</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Lexikon_des_Mittelalters:_Licentia_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lexikon_des_Mittelalters:_Licentia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> However, while the licentia continued to hold a higher prestige than the bachelor's degree (<i>Baccalaureus</i>), it was ultimately reduced to an intermediate step to the <a href="/wiki/Magister_(degree)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magister (degree)">Magister</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctorate</a>, both of which now became the exclusive qualification for teaching.<sup id="cite_ref-Lexikon_des_Mittelalters:_Licentia_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lexikon_des_Mittelalters:_Licentia-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the University, doctoral training was a form of <a href="/wiki/Apprenticeship" title="Apprenticeship">apprenticeship</a> to a <a href="/wiki/Guild" title="Guild">guild</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The traditional term of study before new teachers were admitted to the guild of "Master of Arts", seven years, was the same as the term of apprenticeship for other occupations. Originally the terms "master" and "doctor" were synonymous,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> but over time the doctorate came to be regarded as a higher qualification than the <a href="/wiki/Master_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Master degree">master degree</a>.
</p><p>Today the terms "master", "Doctor" (from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> – meaning literally: "teacher") and "Professor" signify different levels of academic achievement, but in the <a href="/wiki/Medieval_university" title="Medieval university">Medieval university</a> they were equivalent terms, the use of them in the degree name being a matter of custom at a university. (Most universities conferred the Master of Arts, although the highest degree was often termed Master of Theology/Divinity or Doctor of Theology/Divinity depending on the place).
</p><p>The earliest doctoral degrees (<a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theology</a> – Divinitatis Doctor (D.D.), <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">law</a> – Legum Doctor (LL.D., later D.C.L.) and <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a> – Medicinæ Doctor (M.D., D.M.)) reflected the historical separation of all higher University study into these three fields. Over time, the D.D. has gradually become less common outside theology and is now mostly used for honorary degrees, with the title "Doctor of Theology" being used more often for earned degrees. Studies outside <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a> were then called "philosophy", due to the Renaissance conviction that real knowledge could be derived from empirical observation. The degree title of Doctor of Philosophy is a much later time and was not introduced in England before 1900. Studies in what once was called philosophy are now classified as <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">sciences</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/George_Makdisi" title="George Makdisi">George Makdisi</a> theorizes that the <i><a href="/wiki/Ijazah" title="Ijazah">ijazah</a></i> issued in medieval Islamic <a href="/wiki/Madrasa" title="Madrasa">madrasas</a> in the 9th century was the origin of the doctorate that later appeared in medieval European universities.<sup id="cite_ref-Makdisi_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Makdisi-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Guillaume" title="Alfred Guillaume">Alfred Guillaume</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Alatas_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alatas-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Syed_Farid_al-Attas" title="Syed Farid al-Attas">Syed Farid al-Attas</a><sup id="cite_ref-Alatas_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alatas-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Devin_J._Stewart" title="Devin J. Stewart">Devin J. Stewart</a> agree that there is a resemblance between the <i>ijazah</i> and the university degree.<sup id="cite_ref-stewart_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stewart-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Toby_Huff" title="Toby Huff">Toby Huff</a> rejects Makdisi's theory.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bologna" title="University of Bologna">University of Bologna</a> in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, regarded as the oldest university in <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, was the first institution to confer the degree of <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">Doctor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Civil_law_(legal_system)" title="Civil law (legal system)">Civil Law</a> in the late 12th century; it also conferred similar degrees in other subjects, including <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Paris" title="University of Paris">University of Paris</a> used the term "master" for its graduates, a practice adopted by the <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">English</a> universities of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a>, as well as the ancient <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scottish</a> universities of <a href="/wiki/University_of_St_Andrews" title="University of St Andrews">St Andrews</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Aberdeen" title="University of Aberdeen">Aberdeen</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Emergence_of_the_bachelor.27s_degree"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergence_of_the_bachelor's_degree">Emergence of the bachelor's degree</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Emergence of the bachelor&#039;s degree">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Medieval_university" title="Medieval university">medieval European universities</a>, candidates who had completed three or four years of study in the prescribed texts of the <i><a href="/wiki/Trivium_(education)" class="mw-redirect" title="Trivium (education)">trivium</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Grammar" title="Grammar">grammar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhetoric" title="Rhetoric">rhetoric</a> and <a href="/wiki/Logic" title="Logic">logic</a>) and the <i><a href="/wiki/Quadrivium" title="Quadrivium">quadrivium</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Arithmetic" title="Arithmetic">arithmetic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geometry" title="Geometry">geometry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Astronomy" title="Astronomy">astronomy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a>), together known as the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal Arts">Liberal Arts</a> and who had successfully passed examinations held by their master, would be admitted to the degree of <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">Bachelor of Arts</a>, from the Latin <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">baccalaureus</i>, a term previously used of a squire (i.e., apprentice) to a <a href="/wiki/Knight" title="Knight">knight</a>. Further study and in particular successful participation in and then moderating of <a href="/wiki/Disputation" title="Disputation">disputations</a> would earn one the <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Arts" title="Master of Arts">Master of Arts</a> degree, from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <a href="/wiki/Magister_(degree)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magister (degree)">magister</a>, "master" (typically indicating a teacher), entitling one to teach these subjects. Masters of Arts were eligible to enter study under the "higher faculties" of <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">Medicine</a> or <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">Theology</a> and earn first a bachelor's and then master or doctor's degrees in these subjects. Thus a degree was only a step on the way to becoming a fully qualified master – hence the <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> word "graduate", which is based on the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i lang="la" title="Latin language text">gradus</i> ("step").
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_evolution_of_the_terminology_of_degrees">The evolution of the terminology of degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The evolution of the terminology of degrees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The naming of degrees eventually became linked with the subjects studied. Scholars in the faculties of <a href="/wiki/The_arts" title="The arts">arts</a> or <a href="/wiki/Grammar" title="Grammar">grammar</a> became known as "master", but those in <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">law</a> were known as "doctor". As study in the arts or in grammar was a necessary prerequisite to study in subjects such as theology, medicine and law, the degree of doctor assumed a higher status than the <a href="/wiki/Master_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Master degree">master degree</a>. This led to the modern hierarchy in which the <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">Doctor of Philosophy</a> (Ph.D.), which in its present form as a degree based on research and dissertation is a development from 18th- and 19th-century German universities, is a more advanced degree than the <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Arts" title="Master of Arts">Master of Arts</a> (M.A.). The practice of using the term <i>doctor</i> for PhDs developed within German universities and spread across the academic world.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> terminology is tied closely to the original meanings of the terms. The <i><a href="/wiki/Baccalaur%C3%A9at" title="Baccalauréat">baccalauréat</a></i> (cf. "bachelor") is conferred upon French students who have successfully completed their <a href="/wiki/Secondary_education" title="Secondary education">secondary education</a> and admits the student to university. When students graduate from university, they are awarded <i>licence</i>, much as the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">medieval</a> teaching guilds would have done and they are qualified to teach in secondary schools or proceed to higher-level studies. <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> had a similar structure: the term <i>"Bachiller"</i> was used for those who finished the secondary or high-school level education, known as <i>"Bachillerato"</i>. The standard Spanish university 5-years degree was <i>"Licenciado"</i>, (although there were a few 3-years associate degrees called <i>"diplomaturas"</i>, from where the <i>"diplomados"</i> could move to study a related <i>licenciatura</i>). The highest level was "Doctor".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Degrees_awarded_by_institutions_other_than_universities">Degrees awarded by institutions other than universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Degrees awarded by institutions other than universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the past, degrees have also been directly issued by authority of the monarch or by a bishop, rather than any educational institution. This practice has mostly died out. In <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lambeth_Degrees" class="mw-redirect" title="Lambeth Degrees">Lambeth Degrees</a> are still awarded by the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The Archbishop of Canterbury's right to grant degrees is derived from <a href="/wiki/Act_Concerning_Peter%27s_Pence_and_Dispensations" title="Act Concerning Peter&#39;s Pence and Dispensations">Peter's Pence Act of 1533</a> which empowered the Archbishop to grant dispensations previously granted by the Pope.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Among educational institutions, <a href="/wiki/St_David%27s_College,_Lampeter" class="mw-redirect" title="St David&#39;s College, Lampeter">St David's College, Lampeter</a> was granted limited degree awarding powers by <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a> in the nineteenth century, despite not being a university. University College North Staffordshire was also granted degree awarding powers on its foundation in 1949, despite not becoming a university (as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Keele" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Keele">University of Keele</a>) until 1962. Following the <a href="/wiki/Education_Reform_Act_1988" title="Education Reform Act 1988">Education Reform Act 1988</a>, many educational institutions other than universities have been granted degree awarding powers, including higher education colleges and colleges of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a> (many of which are now effectively universities in their own right).<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_dress">Academic dress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Academic dress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Academic_dress" title="Academic dress">Academic dress</a></div>
<p>In most countries, gaining an academic degree entitles the holder to assume distinctive academic dress particular to the awarding institution, identifying the status of the individual wearing them.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Laws_on_granting_and_use_of_degrees">Laws on granting and use of degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Laws on granting and use of degrees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Unaccredited_institutions_of_higher_education" title="Unaccredited institutions of higher education">Unaccredited institutions of higher education</a></div>
<p>In many countries degrees may only be awarded by institutions authorised to do so by the national or regional government. Frequently governments will also regulate the use of <i>university</i> in names of businesses. This approach is followed, for example, by Australia<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The use of fake degrees by individuals, either obtained from a bogus institution or simply invented, is often covered by <a href="/wiki/Fraud" title="Fraud">fraud</a> laws.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Indicating_earned_degrees">Indicating earned degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Indicating earned degrees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Depending on culture and the degree earned, degrees may be indicated by a <a href="/wiki/Pre-nominal_letters#Academic_degrees" title="Pre-nominal letters">pre-nominal title</a>, <a href="/wiki/Post-nominal_letters#Etiquette_for_higher_educational_qualifications" title="Post-nominal letters">post-nominal letters</a>, a choice of either or not indicated at all. In countries influenced by the UK, post-nominal letters are the norm, with only doctorates granting a title, while titles are the norm in many northern European countries.
</p><p>Depending on the culture and the purpose of the listing, only the highest degree, a selection of degrees or all degrees might be listed. The awarding institution may also be shown and it might be specified if a degree was at <a href="/wiki/Honours_degree" title="Honours degree">honours</a> level, particularly where the honours degree is a separate qualification from the ordinary bachelor's degree.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For member institutions of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Commonwealth_Universities" title="Association of Commonwealth Universities">Association of Commonwealth Universities</a>, there is a standard list of abbreviations for university names given in the Commonwealth Universities Yearbook, but in practice many variations are used and the Yearbook notes that the abbreviations used may not match those used by the universities concerned.<sup id="cite_ref-ACU_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACU-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> For some British universities it is traditional to use Latin abbreviations, notably 'Oxon' and 'Cantab' for the Universities of <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">Oxford</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">Cambridge</a> respectively,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> in spite of these having been superseded by English 'Oxf' and 'Camb' in official university usage,<sup id="cite_ref-OxCalendar_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OxCalendar-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> particularly in order to distinguish the <a href="/wiki/Oxbridge_MA" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxbridge MA">Oxbridge MA</a> from an earned MA.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Other Latin abbreviations commonly used include 'Cantuar' for <a href="/wiki/Lambeth_degree" title="Lambeth degree">Lambeth degrees</a> (awarded by the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-OxCalendar_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OxCalendar-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> 'Dunelm' for <a href="/wiki/Durham_University" title="Durham University">Durham University</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> 'Ebor' for the <a href="/wiki/University_of_York" title="University of York">University of York</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and 'Exon' for the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Exeter" title="University of Exeter">University of Exeter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ancient_universities_of_Scotland" title="Ancient universities of Scotland">Ancient universities of Scotland</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a> have abbreviations that are the same in English and Latin. (See <a href="/wiki/Universities_in_the_United_Kingdom#Post-nominal_abbreviations" title="Universities in the United Kingdom">Universities in the United Kingdom §&#160;Post-nominal abbreviations</a> for a more complete list and discussion of abbreviations for British universities.)
</p><p>Confusion can result from universities sharing similar names, e.g. the <a href="/wiki/University_of_York" title="University of York">University of York</a> in the UK and <a href="/wiki/York_University" title="York University">York University</a> in Canada or <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a> in the UK and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Newcastle_(Australia)" title="University of Newcastle (Australia)">University of Newcastle</a> in Australia. In this case, the convention is to include a country abbreviation with the university's name. For example, 'York (Can.)' and 'York (UK)' or 'Newc (UK)' and 'Newc (Aus.) are commonly used to denote degrees conferred by these universities where the potential for confusion exists,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and institution names are given in this form in the Commonwealth Universities Yearbook.<sup id="cite_ref-ACU_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACU-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Abbreviations used for degrees vary between countries and institutions, e.g. MS indicates <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Science" title="Master of Science">Master of Science</a> in the US and places following American usage, but <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Surgery" title="Master of Surgery">Master of Surgery</a> in the UK and most Commonwealth countries, where the standard abbreviation for Master of Science is MSc. Common abbreviations include BA and MA for <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor of arts">Bachelor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Arts" title="Master of Arts">Master of Arts</a>, BS/BSc and MS/MSc for <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">Bachelor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Science" title="Master of Science">Master of Science</a>, MD for <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">Doctor of Medicine</a> and PhD for <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">Doctor of Philosophy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Online_degree">Online degree</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Online degree">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Online_degree" title="Online degree">Online degree</a></div>
<p>An online degree is an academic degree (usually a college degree, but sometimes the term includes high school diplomas and non-degree certificate programs) that can be earned primarily or entirely on a <a href="/wiki/Distance_learning" class="mw-redirect" title="Distance learning">distance learning</a> basis through the use of an Internet-connected computer, rather than attending college in a traditional campus setting. Improvements in technology, the increasing use of the Internet worldwide and the need for people to have flexible school schedules that enable them to work while attending school have led to a proliferation of online colleges that award associate's, bachelor's, master's and doctoral degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Degree_systems_by_regions">Degree systems by regions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Degree systems by regions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span id="Bangladesh.2C_India_and_Pakistan"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bangladesh,_India_and_Pakistan">Bangladesh, India and Pakistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Bangladesh, India and Pakistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Bangladesh and India  mostly follow the <a href="/wiki/Colonial_India" title="Colonial India">colonial era</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> system for classification of degrees. However, Pakistan has recently switched to US model of two years Associate degree and four year Bachelors degree program.  The arts, referring to the performing arts and literature, have the corresponding degrees: Bachelor of Arts (BA) and the Master of Arts (MA). Management degrees are also classified under 'Arts' but is nowadays considered a major new stream, Bachelor of Business Administration (BBA) and Master Of Business Administration (MBA). Science referring to the basic sciences and natural science (Biology, Physics, Chemistry etc.) the corresponding degree are Bachelor of Science (B.Sc.) and its master is called Master of Science (M.Sc.). Another new set of Information Technology degree conferred specially in the field of computer science, Bachelor of Science in Information Technology (B.Sc.IT.) and Master of Science in Information Technology (M.Sc.IT.). The engineering degree in India follows two nomenclatures, <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Engineering" title="Bachelor of Engineering">Bachelor of Engineering</a> (B.E.) and <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Technology" title="Bachelor of Technology">Bachelor of Technology</a> (B.Tech.). Both represent bachelor's degree in engineering. In Pakistan, engineering degrees are <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Engineering" title="Bachelor of Engineering">Bachelor of Engineering</a> (B.E.) and <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science_in_Engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor of Science in Engineering">Bachelor of Science in Engineering</a> (B.S./B.Sc. Engineering). Both are same in curriculum, duration and pattern and differs only in nomenclature where as B.Tech. degree holders are considered as <a href="/wiki/Engineering_technologist" title="Engineering technologist">engineering technologists</a> in Pakistan. The engineering degree in Bangladesh is <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science_in_Engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor of Science in Engineering">Bachelor of Science in Engineering</a> (B.Sc. Engineering). Medical Degree – <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Medicine_%26_Bachelor_of_Surgery" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor of Medicine &amp; Bachelor of Surgery">Bachelor of Medicine &amp; Bachelor of Surgery</a> (MBBS), Dental Degree – <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Dental_Surgery" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor of Dental Surgery">Bachelor of Dental Surgery</a> (BDS), Computer Application Degree – <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Computer_Application" title="Bachelor of Computer Application">Bachelor of Computer Application</a> (BCA) and <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Computer_Application" class="mw-redirect" title="Master of Computer Application">Master of Computer Application</a> (MCA).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sri_Lanka">Sri Lanka</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sri Lanka">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> as many other commonwealth countries follow the British system with its own distinctions. Degrees are approved by the <a href="/wiki/University_Grants_Commission_(Sri_Lanka)" title="University Grants Commission (Sri Lanka)">University Grants Commission</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tunisia">Tunisia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Tunisia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Grading in Tunisia is done on a scale of 0-20. The passing grade is 10 out of 20 which is 50% of the complete mark; 20. This grading system is used from middle-school up to university level. A PhD thesis is even graded out of 20.
</p><p>To get ahead on the academic ladder, one is strictly assessed numerically. That is; if you are a BA holder applying for an MA program you will be admitted according to how high your grades were during your undergraduate years.
</p><p>Level 4 courses come in the form of 1st year of a bachelors programme or HNC (Higher National Certificate). Depending on the Type of associate degree a student may be able to start their 2nd year of bachelors (The course must be the same as the one they are applying for)
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna process">Bologna process</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Higher_Education_Area" title="European Higher Education Area">European Higher Education Area</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_Qualifications_Framework" title="European Qualifications Framework">European Qualifications Framework</a></div>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Recognition_Convention" title="Lisbon Recognition Convention">Convention on the Recognition of Qualifications concerning Higher Education in the European Region</a> in 1997 and the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_declaration" title="Bologna declaration">Bologna declaration</a> in 1999, higher education systems in Europe are being harmonised through the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna process">Bologna process</a>, based on a three-cycle hierarchy of degrees: <i><a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">Bachelor's</a></i>/<i><a href="/wiki/Licentiate_(degree)" title="Licentiate (degree)">Licence</a></i> – <i> <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master&#39;s degree">Master's</a></i> – <i><a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">Doctorate</a></i>, with the later addition of a "short cycle (within the first cycle)" to cover sub-bachelor's qualifications. This system is gradually replacing the two-stage system previously used in some countries and is combined with other elements such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Credit_Transfer_and_Accumulation_System" title="European Credit Transfer and Accumulation System">European Credit Transfer and Accumulation System</a> (ECTS) and the use of <a href="/wiki/Diploma_Supplement" title="Diploma Supplement">Diploma Supplements</a> to make comparisons between qualifications easier.
</p><p>The European Higher Education Area (EHEA) was formally established in 2010 and as of September 2016 has 50 members.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Implementation of the various elements of the EHEA varies. Twenty-four countries have fully implemented a national qualifications framework and a further ten have a framework but have not yet certified it against the <a href="/wiki/QF-EHEA" title="QF-EHEA">overarching framework</a>; in 38 countries <a href="/wiki/European_Credit_Transfer_and_Accumulation_System" title="European Credit Transfer and Accumulation System">ECTS credits</a> are used for all higher education programmes; 31 countries have fully implemented diploma supplements; and only 11 countries have included all the major points of the <a href="/wiki/Lisbon_Recognition_Convention" title="Lisbon Recognition Convention">Lisbon Recognition Convention</a> in national legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 2008, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> has been developing the <a href="/wiki/European_Qualifications_Framework" title="European Qualifications Framework">European Qualifications Framework</a> (EQF). This is an eight-level framework designed to allow cross-referencing of the various national qualifications frameworks. While it is not specific to higher education, the top four levels (5–8) correspond to the short cycle, first cycle, second cycle and third cycle of the EHEA.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Austria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, there are currently two parallel systems of academic degrees:
</p>
<ul><li>the traditional two-cycle system of <a href="/wiki/Magister_(degree)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magister (degree)">Magister</a>/<a href="/wiki/Diplom" title="Diplom">Diplom</a> followed by the <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">Doctorate</a> and</li>
<li>the three-cycle system of <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">Bachelor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Master_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Master degree">Master</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">Doctorate</a> as defined by the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna process">Bologna process</a>.</li></ul>
<p>With a few exceptions, the two-cycle degree system will be phased out by 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Some of the established degree naming has, however, been preserved, allowing universities to award the "Diplom-Ingenieur" (and for a while also the "Magister") to graduates of the new-style Master programmes.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Czech_Republic">Czech Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Czech Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Czech Republic implemented Bologna process so there are basically three degrees: Bachelor (3 years), Master (2 years after Bachelor) and Doctor (3 years after Master).
</p><p>There are also voluntary academic titles called "small doctorates" (e. g. RNDr. for natural sciences, PhDr. for philosophy, JUDr. for law etc.) achieved after rigorosum exam. Medical students don't get bachelor's or master's degrees, instead they study six years and after obligatory rigorous exam they get title MUDr. <span class="cleanup-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">(equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">MD</a> degree)</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="&quot;MD degree&quot; in the US sense of a primary medical qualification or the UK sense of a research degree in medicine or a different meaning from somewhere else? (October 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> or MDDr. for dentists or MVDr. for veterinary physicians. They can also get "big doctorate" (<a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">Ph.D.</a>) after another three or (more often) four years of studies.
</p><p>Bachelor's degrees, master's degrees and small doctorates in the form of shortcuts (Bc., Mgr., Ing., ...) are listed before name of person, Doctor degree (Ph.D.) is listed after name (e. g. MUDr. Jan Novák, Ph.D.). There are more <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Czech_Republic#Tertiary_education" title="Education in the Czech Republic">degrees</a> that used to be awarded, but you can still encounter them. <span class="cleanup-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">Czechs are very proud of their academic degrees and titles therefore its omission is considered disrespectful.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="This is certainly not a generally valid rule. In academia, it is usual to use doctoral and higher degrees/titles when speaking to someone, but I have never seen anyone using and/or demanding usage of bachelor or master. In this case, it is more common to use general &#39;pan/pane&#39; for males, &#39;paní&#39; for married female or a woman who has some degree or &#39;slečna/slečno&#39; for an unmarried woman without a degree. I am not aware that people usually use their titles outside academia (or schools). Printed and formal documents is a different case though, AFAIK lots of people tend to use their full titles (this may include e.g. visiting cards). (March 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna process">Bologna process</a></div>
<p>Before the adaptation to international standards, the lowest degree that would normally be studied at universities in <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> was equivalent to a master's degree (<i>kandidatgrad</i>). Officially, bachelor's degrees was always obtained after 3 years' university studies.
</p><p>Various medium-length (2–4 years) professional degrees have been adapted so they now have status as professional bachelor's degrees of varying length and opposed to academic bachelor's degrees they are considered to be "applied" degrees. A professional bachelor's degree is 180 or 210 or 240 ECTS-points.<sup id="cite_ref-ufm.dk_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ufm.dk-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The academic degrees available at universities are:<sup id="cite_ref-ufm.dk_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ufm.dk-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><i>bachelor i &lt;field of study&gt;</i> (bachelor's degree = 180 ECTS-points)</li>
<li><i>cand. &lt;Latin abbreviation of field of study&gt;</i> (master's degree = 120 ECTS-points, except Medicine, which is 180 ECTS-points and Veterinary Medicine, which is 150 ECTS-points)</li>
<li><i>ph.d.</i> (PhD degree = normally 180 ECTS-points)</li>
<li><i>dr. &lt;Latin abbreviation of field of study&gt;</i> (higher doctoral degree = normally after a minimum of 5 years of individual and original research)</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Finland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Historically, the Finnish higher education system is derived from the German system. The current system of higher education comprises two types of higher education institutions, the universities and the polytechnics, many of whom refer to themselves as Universities of Applied Sciences (UAS)<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> With the exception of few fields such as Medicine and Dentistry, the Finnish system of Higher education degrees is in compliance with the Bologna process. Universities award bachelor's degrees (<i>kandidaatti / kandidat</i>), Master's degrees (<i>maisteri / magister</i>) and doctoral degrees (<i>lisensiaatin tutkinto / licentiat examen</i> and <i>tohtorin tutkinto / doktorexamen</i>). In most fields the system of doctoral degrees is two-tier, the degree of Licentiate is an independent academic degree but completing the degree of Doctor does not require completion of a Licentiate degree. The Polytechnics (Universities of Applied Sciences) have the right to award bachelor's and master's degrees, the degree titles of are distinct from the titles used for university degrees.
</p><p>In general, students who are admitted to bachelor studies at a university have the right to continue to studies at master level. At polytechnics, the right to continue to master-level studies has to be applied for separately and there is also a work experience requirement. The majority of master's degree holders have graduated from university.
</p><p>The degrees awarded by the universities and polytechnics are at par by law, but the content and orientation of studies is different. A master's degree obtained at a polytechnic gives the same academic right to continue studies at Doctoral level as a master's degree obtained at a university.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France">France</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: France">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<tr>
<th>Licence
</th>
<td style="text-align:center;">Licenciate's Diploma
</td>
<td style="text-align:center;"><i>diplôme de formation générale</i> (<a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midwifery" title="Midwifery">Midwifery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odontology" class="mw-redirect" title="Odontology">Odontology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmacy" title="Pharmacy">Pharmacy</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><br />Nurse State Diploma<br /><a href="/wiki/Ergotherapy" class="mw-redirect" title="Ergotherapy">Ergotherapist</a> State Diploma<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</td>
<td style="text-align:center;"><i>diplôme de comptabilité et de gestion</i><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>

<td style="text-align:center;"><i>diplôme d’études en architecture</i><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><br />Undergraduate diplomas of the <a href="/wiki/Conservatoire_national_sup%C3%A9rieur_de_musique_et_de_danse_de_Paris" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservatoire national supérieur de musique et de danse de Paris">conservatoire national supérieur de musique et de danse de Paris</a>

</td>
<td style="text-align:center;">Diploma of the <a href="/wiki/%C3%89cole_militaire_interarmes" title="École militaire interarmes">école militaire interarmes</a><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>

<tr>
<th>Baccalaureate
</th>
<td style="text-align:center;" colspan="10">Bachelor's Diploma
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The French national education system makes a distinction between a <i>diplôme national</i> ("national degree") and <i><a href="/wiki/Dipl%C3%B4me_universitaire" title="Diplôme universitaire">diplôme universitaire</a></i> ("university degree"). The former, which are considered higher status, are controlled by the state and issued by universities on behalf of the responsible ministry; the latter are controlled and granted by the universities themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, private providers may be recognised by the state and then, after five years of recognition, have their degrees validated by the state, the validation having to be renewed every six years.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Historically, academic degrees were orientated towards research and the vocational education system awarded only diplomas. Since the implementation of the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Process" title="Bologna Process">Bologna Process</a> in France, things are going towards a simplification: schools continue to deliver their own diplomas, but the State recognition and degree awarding is far more ranged than before. Diploma courses such as the Technological University Diploma (<i>diplôme universitaire de technologie</i>; DUT) and the Technologist's Certificate (<i>brevet de technician supérieur</i>; BTS) are now recognised as "short cycle" qualifications worth 120 <a href="/wiki/European_Credit_Transfer_and_Accumulation_System" title="European Credit Transfer and Accumulation System">ECTS</a> credits, allowing progression from these to academic qualifications.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, there are diplomas in France with no degree recognition, e.g. specific diplomas designed by various institutions with no recognition from the Ministry of Education, such as the <a href="/wiki/Mast%C3%A8re_sp%C3%A9cialis%C3%A9" title="Mastère spécialisé">mastère spécialisé</a><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> or the <a href="/wiki/Sciences_Po" title="Sciences Po">Sciences Po</a> <i>Bachelor</i>.
</p><p>The recognised degrees fall in three levels, following the <a href="/wiki/QF-EHEA" title="QF-EHEA">Qualifications Framework of the European Higher Education Area</a>. These are the <i>licence</i> (first cycle), <i>master</i> (second cycle) and <i>doctorat</i> (third cycle). All licence degrees are 3 years (180 ECTS credits) in length and all master's degrees are 2 years (120 ECTS credits) in length. There are also 5 year (300 ECTS credits) <a href="/wiki/Engineer%27s_degree" title="Engineer&#39;s degree">engineer's degrees</a>, which are master's degree. In addition to the doctorate, which is always a research degree, the <i>Diplôme d'Etat de docteur en médicine</i> and the <i>Diplôme d'Etat de docteur vétérinaire</i> are also considered third cycle qualifications.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Traditionally in Germany, students graduated after four to six years either with a <i><a href="/wiki/Magister_degree" title="Magister degree">Magister</a></i> degree in <a href="/wiki/Social_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Social Sciences">Social Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">Humanities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">Linguistics</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="Arts">Arts</a> or with a <i><a href="/wiki/Diplom" title="Diplom">Diplom</a></i> degree in <a href="/wiki/Natural_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural Sciences">Natural Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economics" title="Economics">Economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Business_Administration" class="mw-redirect" title="Business Administration">Business Administration</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="Political Science">Political Science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sociology" title="Sociology">Sociology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">Theology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">Engineering</a>. Those degrees were the first and at the same time highest non-<a href="/wiki/PhD" class="mw-redirect" title="PhD">PhD</a>/<a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">Doctorate</a>-title in many disciplines before its gradual replacement by other Anglo-Saxon-inspired master's and bachelor's degrees under the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna process">Bologna process</a>. The <i>Magister</i> and <i>Diplom</i> awarded by universities, both of which require a final thesis, are considered equivalent to a master's degree, although the <i>Diplom</i> awarded by a <a href="/wiki/Fachhochschule" title="Fachhochschule"><i>Fachhochschule</i> (university of applied sciences)</a> is at bachelor's degree level.<sup id="cite_ref-German_education_system_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-German_education_system-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A special kind of examination is the <i><a href="/wiki/Staatsexamen" title="Staatsexamen">Staatsexamen</a></i> (State Examination). It is not an academic degree but a government <a href="/wiki/Licensure" title="Licensure">licensing examination</a> that future doctors, dentists, teachers, lawyers (solicitors), judges, public prosecutors, patent attorneys and pharmacists have to pass in order to be eligible to work in their profession. Students usually study at university for three to six year, depending on the field, before they take the first Staatsexamen. While this is normally at master's level, a few courses (e.g. primary and lower secondary level teaching), which have a standard study period of three years, are assigned to bachelor's level.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>  After the first Staatsexamen, teachers and lawyers go through a form of <a href="/wiki/Pupillage" title="Pupillage">pupillage</a>, the <i>Vorbereitungsdienst</i>, for two years, before they are able to take the second Staatsexamen, which tests their practical abilities in their jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-German_education_system_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-German_education_system-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> At some institutions pharmacists and jurists can choose whether to be awarded the first Staatsexamen or a master's degree (or formerly the <i>Diplom</i>).
</p><p>Since 1999, the traditional degrees have been replaced by <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">bachelor's</a> (<i>Bachelor</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master&#39;s degree">master's</a> (<i>Master</i>) degrees as part of the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process#Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna process">Bologna process</a>. The main reasons for this change are to make degrees internationally comparable and to introduce degrees to the German system which take less time to complete (German students typically took five years or more to earn a <i>Magister</i> or <i>Diplom</i>). Some universities were initially resistant to this change, considering it a displacement of a venerable tradition for the pure sake of globalization. However, universities had to fulfill the new standard by the end of 2007. Enrollment into <i><a href="/wiki/Diplom" title="Diplom">Diplom</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Magister_(degree)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magister (degree)">Magister</a></i> programs is no longer possible. However, programs leading to <i>Staatsexamen</i> did usually not make the transition to Bologna degrees.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">Doctorates</a> are issued with various designations, depending on the faculty: e.g., Doktor der Naturwissenschaften (Doctor of Natural Science); Doktor der Rechtswissenschaften (Doctor of Law); Doktor der Medizin (Doctor of Medicine); Doktor der Philosophie (Doctor of Philosophy), to name just a few. Multiple doctorates and honorary doctorates are often listed and even used in forms of address in German-speaking countries. A Diplom, Magister, Master's or Staatsexamen student can proceed to a doctorate. Well qualified bachelor's graduates can also enrol directly into PhD programs after a procedure to determine their aptitude administered by the admitting university.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The doctoral degree (e.g., Dr. rer. nat., Dr. phil. and others) is the highest academic degree in Germany and generally a research degree. The degree <i>Dr. med.</i> for <a href="/wiki/Medical_doctor" class="mw-redirect" title="Medical doctor">medical doctors</a> has to be viewed differently; medical students usually write their doctoral theses right after they have completed studies, without any previous conducted scientific research, just as students in other disciplines write a <i>Diplom</i>, <i>Magister</i> or <i>Master's</i> thesis.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Higher doctorates, such as the D.Sc. degree in the UK, are not present in the German system.
</p><p>However, sometimes incorrectly regarded as a degree, the <a href="/wiki/Habilitation" title="Habilitation">Habilitation</a> is a higher academic qualification in Germany, Austria and Switzerland that allows further teaching and research endorsement after a doctorate. It is earned by writing a second thesis (the <i>Habilitationsschrift</i>) or presenting a portfolio of first-author publications in an advanced topic. The exact requirements for satisfying a Habilitation depend on individual universities. The "habil.", as it is abbreviated to represent that a habilitation has been awarded after the doctorate, was traditionally the conventional qualification for serving at least as a <i>Privatdozent</i> (e.g. "PD Dr. habil.") (Senior Lecturer) in an academic professorship. Some German universities no longer require the Habilitation, although preference may still be given to applicants who have this credential, for academic posts in the more traditional fields.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Ireland</a> operates under a National Framework of Qualifications (NFQ).
The school leaving qualification attained by students is called the Leaving Certificate. It is considered Level 4-5 on the framework. This qualification is the traditional route of entry into third level education. There are also Level 5 qualifications in certain vocational subjects (e.g. Level 5 Certificate in Restaurant Operations) awarded by the Further Education and Training Awards Council (FETAC). Advanced Certificates at level 6 are also awarded by FETAC.
</p><p>The Higher Education and Training Awards Council (HETAC) award the following:
A higher certificate at Level 6;
An ordinary bachelor's degree at Level 7;
An honours bachelor's degree or <a href="/wiki/Higher_diploma" title="Higher diploma">higher diploma</a> at Level 8;
A master's degree or postgraduate diploma at Level 9;
A doctoral degree or higher doctorate at level 10.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
These are completed in institutes of technology or universities.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_in_Italy" title="Higher education in Italy">Higher education in Italy</a></div>
<p>In Italy access to university is possible after gaining the <i><a href="/wiki/Diploma" title="Diploma">Diploma</a> di <a href="/wiki/Maturit%C3%A0" class="mw-redirect" title="Maturità">Maturità</a></i> at 19 years of age, following 5 years of study in a specific high school focused on certain subjects (e.g. <i>liceo classico</i> focused on classical subjects, including philosophy, ancient Greek and Latin; <i>liceo scientifico</i> focused on scientific subjects such as <a href="/wiki/Maths" class="mw-redirect" title="Maths">Maths</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">Chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">Biology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">Physics</a> but also including philosophy, ancient Latin and Italian Literature; <i>liceo linguistico</i> focused on Foreign Languages and Literature; <i>istituto tecnico</i> focused on practical and theoretical subjects such as <a href="/wiki/Mechanics" title="Mechanics">Mechanics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aerospace" title="Aerospace">Aerospace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">Shipbuilding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">Electronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">Computer science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecommunications">Telecommunications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">Chemistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">Biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fashion_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Fashion industry">Fashion industry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">Food industry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Building_technology" class="mw-redirect" title="Building technology">Building technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Law" title="Law">Law</a> and <a href="/wiki/Economy" title="Economy">Economy</a>).
</p><p>After gaining the diploma one can enter university and enrol in any curriculum (e.g. physics, medicine, chemistry, engineering, architecture): all high school diplomas allow access to any university curriculum, although most universities have pre-admission tests.
</p><p>In 2011, Italy introduced a qualifications framework, known as the <i>Quadro dei Titoli Italiani</i> (QTI), tied to the three cycles of the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Process" title="Bologna Process">Bologna Process</a>. This tied together in a three-level system both the new qualifications introduced as part of the Bologna process and the older, pre-Bologna qualifications and covers qualifications from university institutions and higher education institutions for fine arts, music and dance (AFAM institutions).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In addition to academic degrees, many professional qualifications are tied to the QTI at the different levels.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first level, tied to the first cycle of the Bologna Process, covers the <i><a href="/wiki/Laurea" title="Laurea">laurea</a></i> (bachelor's degree) in universities and the <i>Diploma accademico di primo livello</i> in AFAM institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_new_quals_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_new_quals-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The older qualifications mapped to this level are the <i>Diploma universitario</i> and the <i>Diploma di scuole dirette a fini speciali (SDAFS)</i> from universities and the <i>Diploma di Conservatorio</i>, <i>Diploma di Istituto Musicale Pareggiato</i>, <i>Diploma dell'Accademia di Belle Arti</i>, <i>Diploma dell'Istituto Superiore delle Industrie Artistiche (ISIA)</i>, <i>Diploma dell'Accademia Nazionale di Danza</i> and <i>Diploma dell'Accademia Nazionale di Arte Drammatica</i> from AFAM institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_old_quals_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_old_quals-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The <i>laurea</i> is obtained after three years of study (180 ECTS credits) and gives the academic title of <i>dottore</i>;<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_new_quals_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_new_quals-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> the older university qualifications at this level took two to three years, with three year courses granting the title of <i>dottore</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_old_quals_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_old_quals-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The second level, tied to the second cycle of the Bologna Process, covers the <i>Laurea magistrale</i> and the <i>laurea specialistica</i> in university institutions and the <i>Diploma accademico di secondo livello</i> in AFAM institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_new_quals_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_new_quals-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The old <i>Diploma di laurea</i> is mapped to this level.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_old_quals_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_old_quals-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Laurea magistrale</i> and the <i>laurea specialistica</i> are obtained after two further years of study (120 ECTS credits) and give the academic title of <i>dottore magistrale</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_new_quals_67-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_new_quals-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The old <i>Diploma di laurea</i> took four to six years but was accessed directly from school, with a possible reduction by one year for those with a related <i>diploma</i> and also granted the title of <i>dottore magistrale</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_old_quals_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_old_quals-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The third level, tied to the third cycle of the Bologna Process, covers the <i>Dottorato di ricerca</i> in university institutions and the <i>Diploma accademico di formazione alla ricerca</i> in AFAM institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_new_quals_67-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_new_quals-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The old <i>Dottorato di ricerca</i> and <i>Diploma di specializzazione</i> are tied to this level.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_old_quals_68-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_old_quals-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Dottorato di ricerca</i>, under both new and old systems, takes a minimum of three years after the <i>laurea magistralie/specialistica</i> and gives the academic titles of <i>Dottore di Ricerca (Dott. Ric.)</i> and PhD.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_new_quals_67-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_new_quals-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-QTI_old_quals_68-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_old_quals-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The old <i>Diploma di specializzazione</i> took two to six years and gave the academic title of <i>Specialista</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_old_quals_68-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_old_quals-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Universities in Italy offer a number of other qualifications including the <i>Master universitario di primo livello</i> (1 year/60 ECTS credits, 2nd cycle qualification) and the <i>Master universitario di secondo livello</i> (1 year/60 ECTS credits, 3rd cycle qualification), following on from the <i>laurea</i> and the <i>laurea magistrale/specialistica</i> respectively. These do not give access to the PhD. The <i>Diploma di specializzazione</i>, which is offered in a few specific professions, takes two to six years and gives the title of <i>specialista</i>. The <i>Diploma di perfezionamento</i> is a university certificate, aimed at professional training or in specific study fields, which usually takes one year; it is not allocated a level on the framework.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_other_quals_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_other_quals-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>AFAM institutions may offer <i>Diploma di perfezionamento o Master</i> and <i>Diploma accademico di specializzazione</i>. These are one year and two year qualifications respectively and may be offered at second cycle or third cycle level, distinguished by adding <i>(I)</i> or <i>(II)</i> after the qualification name. Higher Schools for Language Mediators offer the <i>Diploma di mediatore linguistico</i>, a first cycle degree taking three years (180 ECTS credits), which gives access to the <i>laurea specialistica</i>. Specialisation Institutes/Schools in Psychoterapy offer the <i>Diploma di specializzazione in psicoterapia</i>, a third cycle qualification taking at least four years and requiring a <i>laurea magistrale/specialistica</i> in either Psychology or Medicine and Surgery, along with professional registration.<sup id="cite_ref-QTI_other_quals_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QTI_other_quals-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Netherlands">Netherlands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Netherlands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Netherlands" title="Education in the Netherlands">Education in the Netherlands</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, the structure of academic studies was altered significantly in 1982 when the "<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tweefasenstructuur" class="extiw" title="nl:Tweefasenstructuur">Tweefasenstructuur</a>" (Two Phase Structure) was introduced by the Dutch Minister of Education, <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wim_Deetman" class="extiw" title="nl:Wim Deetman">Wim Deetman</a>. With this two phase structure an attempt was made to standardise all the different studies and structure them to an identical timetable. Additional effect was that students would be persuaded stringently to produce results within a preset time-frame or otherwise discontinue their studies. The two phase structure has been adapted to a bachelor-master structure as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna process">Bologna process</a>.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Admission">Admission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Admission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In order for a Dutch student to get access to a university education, the student must complete a six-year pre-university secondary education called "<i><a href="/wiki/Voorbereidend_wetenschappelijk_onderwijs" title="Voorbereidend wetenschappelijk onderwijs">voorbereidend wetenschappelijk onderwijs</a></i>" (vwo). There are other routes possible, but only if the end level of the applicant is comparable to the two levels is access to university education is granted. For some studies, specific end levels or disciplines are required, e.g., graduating without <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">chemistry</a> will make it impossible to study <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>. People 21 years old or older who do not have the required entrance diplomas may opt for an entrance exam for being admitted to a higher education curriculum. In this exam, they have to prove their command of disciplines considered necessary for pursuing such study. After September 1, 2002 they would be thus admitted to a Bachelor's curriculum, not to a Master's curriculum.
</p><p>For some studies<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> in the Netherlands, a governmental determined <a href="/wiki/Numerus_clausus" title="Numerus clausus">limited access</a> is in place (although under political review for abolishment, February 2011).<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> This is a limitation of the number of applicants to a specific study, thus trying to control the eventual number of graduates. The most renowned studies for their <a href="/wiki/Numerus_clausus" title="Numerus clausus">numerus clausus</a> are medicine and dentistry. Every year a combination of the highest pre-university graduation grades and some additional conditions determine who can start such a <a href="/wiki/Numerus_clausus" title="Numerus clausus">numerus clausus</a> study and who can not.
</p><p>Almost all <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_the_Netherlands" title="List of universities in the Netherlands">Dutch universities</a> are government supported universities, with only very few privately owned universities in existence (i.e. one in <a href="/wiki/Nyenrode_Business_Universiteit" class="mw-redirect" title="Nyenrode Business Universiteit">business</a> and all others in <a href="/wiki/Theology" title="Theology">theology</a>). <a href="/wiki/Leiden_University" title="Leiden University">Leiden University</a> is the oldest, founded in 1575.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Bologna_phases">Pre-Bologna phases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Pre-Bologna phases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Before the introduction of the bachelor-master structure, almost all academic studies in the Netherlands had the same length of four years and had two phases:
</p>
<ul><li><i>The "<a href="/wiki/Propaedeutics" title="Propaedeutics">propedeutische</a> fase" (1–2 years):</i> After finishing this phase a student can follow another two years' study, which grants equivalents to the Anglo-Saxon BSc (<a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">Bachelor of Science</a>), BA (<a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">Bachelor of Arts</a>) or LLB (<a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Laws" title="Bachelor of Laws">Bachelor of Laws</a>).</li>
<li><i>The "doctorale fase" (3–4 years):</i> Completing the first phase successfully gives the student access to the second phase. Again, failure to finish within the time given will lead to discontinuation. This phase is concluded with the "<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctoraalexamen" class="extiw" title="nl:Doctoraalexamen">doctoraal examen</a>" (doctoral exam). This is not similar to any type of doctoral exam that would grant the student with any type of <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">PhD</a> title. Successful completion however does grant the student the Dutch degree of "drs." "<a href="/wiki/Doctorandus" title="Doctorandus">doctorandus</a>", ir. ("ingenieur" – engineer) or "mr." ("Meester in de rechten" - master of law). Nowadays these Dutch titles have been largely replaced by the Anglo Saxon titles MSc (<a href="/wiki/Master_of_Science" title="Master of Science">Master of Science</a>), MA (<a href="/wiki/Master_of_Arts" title="Master of Arts">Master of Arts</a>) and LLM (<a href="/wiki/LLM" class="mw-redirect" title="LLM">Master of Laws</a>), depending on the area of study.</li></ul>
<p>For medical students the "<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctorandus" class="extiw" title="nl:Doctorandus">doctorandus</a>" degree is not equivalent to the European Anglo Saxon postgraduate research degree in medicine of MD (<a href="/wiki/Medical_Doctor" class="mw-redirect" title="Medical Doctor">Medical Doctor</a>). Besides the title doctorandus, the graduates of the Curius curriculum may also bear the title <i>arts</i> (physician). The doctorandus in medicine title is granted after four years (nominal time) of the Curius curriculum, while the title physician is granted after six years (nominal time) of that curriculum. The Dutch physician title is equal to a MSc degree according to the Bologna process and can be compared with the MBBS in the UK degree system and the North American MD, but not the UK MD degree, which is a research degree. One-on-one equivalence or interchangeability of the Dutch medical title and MD is often suggested. However, officially the MD title is not known, nor legal to use in the Netherlands. The correct notation for a Dutch physician who completed his or her medical studies, but did not pursue a doctor (<a href="/wiki/PhD" class="mw-redirect" title="PhD">PhD</a>-like) study is "drs."
