(e.g. <i>drs. Jansen, arts</i>) and not "dr." in medicine, as often used incorrectly. However, like in the United Kingdom, physicians holding these degrees are referred to as 'Doctor' by courtesy. In the Netherlands, there is the informal title <i>dokter</i> for physicians, but not <i>doctor</i> (dr.), unless they also earn such degree by completing a PhD curriculum. Furthermore, the "<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctorandus" class="extiw" title="nl:Doctorandus">doctorandus</a>" degree does not give a medical student the right to treat patients; for this a minimum of two years additional study (internships) is required. After obtaining a Medical Board registration, Dutch physicians must work an additional two to six years in a field of expertise to become a registered medical specialist. Dutch surgeons commonly are only granted access to surgeon training and positions after obtaining a doctorate (PhD) successfully. In recent years, the six-year (nominal time) old Curius curriculum (which offered the titles doctorandus and physician) has been replaced with a three-year (nominal time) Bachelor Curius+ followed by a three-year (nominal time) Master Curius+. Those who had already begun their old-style Curius curriculum before that will still have to complete it as a six-year study (nominal time).
</p><p>A <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctorandus" class="extiw" title="nl:Doctorandus">doctorandus</a> in law uses the title "<i>meester</i>" (master, abbreviated as <i>mr. Jansen</i>) instead of drs. and some studies like for example technique and agriculture grant the title "<i>ingenieur</i>" (engineer, noted as <i>ir. Jansen</i>) instead of drs. These titles as equivalent to an LL.M (the title mr.) and to a MSc (the title ir.) and if got before September 1, 2002 from a recognized Dutch university, may be rendered as M (from Master) behind one's name, instead of using the typical Dutch shortcuts before one's name. Since September 1, 2002, Dutch universities offer specific BSc, BA or LLB studies followed by MSc, MA or LLM studies, thus integrating into and merging with the international scientific community, offering lectures, other classes, seminars or complete curricula in English instead of Dutch. According to their field of study, MSc graduates may use either ir. or drs. before their names, MA graduates may use drs. before their name and LLM graduates may use mr. before their names, but only if they received such degrees from recognized Dutch universities.
</p><p>Not uncommonly, the Dutch "drs." abbreviation can cause much confusion in other countries, since it is perceived as a person who has a <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">PhD</a> in multiple disciplines. In the Netherlands, the degree <a href="/wiki/MPhil" class="mw-redirect" title="MPhil">MPhil</a> is not legally recognised.
</p><p>After successfully obtaining a "drs.", "ir." or "mr." degree, a student has the opportunity to follow a promotion study (informally called <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">PhD</a>) to eventually obtain a doctorate and subsequently the title "doctor". Promotion studies are structured ideally according to a preset time schedule of 4 to 6 years, during which the student has to be mentored by at least one <a href="/wiki/Professor" title="Professor">professor</a>. The promotion study has to be concluded with at least a scientific thesis, which has to be defended to "a gathering of his/her peers", in practice the Board of the <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(division)" title="Faculty (division)">Faculty</a> with guest professors from other faculties and/or universities added. More and more common and in some disciplines even mandatory, is that the student writes and submits scientific publications to peer-reviewed journals, which eventually need to be accepted for publication. The number of publications is often debated and varies considerably between the various disciplines. However, in all disciplines the student is obligated to produce and publish a dissertation or thesis in book form.
</p>
<h5><span id="Bachelor.2Fmaster_structure"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bachelor/master_structure">Bachelor/master structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Bachelor/master structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>All current Dutch academic education programs are offered in the Anglo-Saxon bachelor/master structure. It takes three years to earn a bachelor's degree and another one or two years to earn a master's degree. There are three official academic bachelor titles (BA, BSc and LLB) and three official master titles (MA, MSc and LLM). These academic titles are protected by the Dutch government.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_title_bearing">Academic title bearing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Academic title bearing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>After obtaining a doctorate, Dutch doctors may bear either the title dr. (lower case) before or the letter D following their name, but not both simultaneously.<sup id="cite_ref-rijksoverheid_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rijksoverheid-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> There is no specific notation of the discipline in which the doctorate is obtained.
</p><p>Stacking of the titles as seen in countries such as Germany (Prof. Dr. Dr. Dr. Gruber) is highly uncommon in the Netherlands and not well received culturally. Those who have multiple doctor titles may use dr.mult. before their name, but this is seldomly seen in practice.<sup id="cite_ref-rijksoverheid_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rijksoverheid-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The honoris cause doctors may use dr.h.c. before their name.<sup id="cite_ref-rijksoverheid_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rijksoverheid-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Combining different Dutch titles, especially in different disciplines, is allowed however (e.g. mr. dr. Jansen, dr. mr. Jansen, dr. ir. Jansen, mr. ir. drs. Jansen, mr. ir. Jansen). The use of the combination ir. ing. is frequent, indicating one holds a <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Netherlands#Hbo" title="Education in the Netherlands">HBO</a>, vocational (or professional) engineering degree together with an academic engineering degree.<sup id="cite_ref-onzetaal.nl_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onzetaal.nl-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> What is not allowed is, after obtaining a doctorate, using dr. drs. Jansen; dr. Jansen should be used instead.
</p><p>A combination of a Dutch title with an international title is not allowed, except for some limited number of international professional titles.<sup id="cite_ref-onzetaal.nl_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onzetaal.nl-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Thus, one should choose either one's classical Dutch title or use the shortcut provided by the law following one's name (since September 1, 2002 it is the other way around: those who hold Dutch degrees as MSc, LLM or MA may optionally use the old-style shortcuts before their names).<sup id="cite_ref-onzetaal.nl_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onzetaal.nl-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-burgervragen_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-burgervragen-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Hence, formal use of the Anglo-Saxon <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">PhD</a> following one's name is not legal, as it is not a Dutch degree. However, its use is commonly used for clarity towards international readers, for example English publications. The law provides the option of using the shortcut D following one's name instead of dr. before one's name.
</p><p>"<i>Doctors</i>" (dr.) can proceed to teach at universities as "<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universitair_docent" class="extiw" title="nl:Universitair docent">universitair docent</a>" (UD – <a href="/wiki/Assistant_professor" title="Assistant professor">assistant professor</a>). With time, experience and/ or achievement, this can evolve to a position as "<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universitair_hoofddocent" class="extiw" title="nl:Universitair hoofddocent">universitair hoofddocent</a>" (UHD – <a href="/wiki/Associate_professor" title="Associate professor">associate professor</a>). Officially an UHD still works under the supervision of a "<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hoogleraar" class="extiw" title="nl:Hoogleraar">hoogleraar</a>", the head of the department and commonly a <a href="/wiki/Professor" title="Professor">professor</a>. However, this is not a given; it is also possible that a department is headed by a "plain" doctor, based on knowledge, achievement and expertise. The position of "<a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hoogleraar" class="extiw" title="nl:Hoogleraar">hoogleraar</a>" is the highest possible scientific position at a university and equivalent to the US "full" professor. The Dutch <a href="/wiki/Professor" title="Professor">professor</a>'s title, noted as <i>prof. Jansen</i> or <i>professor Jansen</i>, is connected to one's employment. This means that, should the <a href="/wiki/Professor" title="Professor">professor</a> leave the <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a>, he or she also loses the privilege to use the title of <a href="/wiki/Professor" title="Professor">professor</a>. Retired professors are an exception and may continue to note the title in front of their name or use the title emeritus professor (em. prof.). People who switch to a non-university job lose their professor title and are only allowed to use the "dr." abbreviation.
</p><p>Unlike some other European countries such as Germany, Dutch academic titles are used rarely outside academia, hold no value in everyday life and typically are not listed on official documentation (e.g. passport, drivers license, (governmental) communication). Dutch academic titles however are legally protected and can only be used by graduates from Dutch institutions of higher education. Illegal use is considered a misdemeanor and subject to legal prosecution.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Holders of foreign degrees therefore need special permission before being able to use a recognised Dutch title, but they are free to use their own foreign title (untranslated).<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> In practice, the Public Department does not prosecute the illegal use of a protected title (in the Netherlands applies the <a href="/wiki/Principle_of_opportunity" title="Principle of opportunity">principle of opportunity</a>, so some known crimes are not prosecuted).<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Norway">Norway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Norway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Prior to 1980, there were around 50 different degrees and corresponding education programs within the Norwegian higher education system. 
Degrees had titles that included the gender based Latin term <i>candidatus/candidata</i>. The second part of the title usually consisted of a Latin word corresponding to the profession or training. For example, Cand. Mag. (Candidatus Magisterii) required 4 to 5 years, Cand. Real.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> (Candidatus Realium) required 6 years of study and a scientific thesis in a select set of scientific disciplines (realia). Over the years these were replaced gradually with degrees that were more and more internationally comparable programs and corresponding titles. For example, the degree Cand. Scient. replaced Cand. Real. in the period 1985 to 2003. These degrees were all retired in 2003 in favour of an international system.
</p><p>The reform of higher education in Norway, <i>Kvalitetsreformen</i> (<i>"The Quality Reform"</i>), was passed in the Norwegian Parliament, the <a href="/wiki/Stortinget" class="mw-redirect" title="Stortinget">Storting</a>, in 2001 and carried out during the 2003/2004 academic year. It introduced standard periods of study and the titles <i>master</i> and <i>bachelor (<a href="/wiki/Baccalaureus" class="mw-redirect" title="Baccalaureus">baccalaureus</a>)</i>.
</p><p>The system differentiates between a free master's degree and a master's degree in <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a>. The latter corresponds to the former <i>sivilingeniør</i> degree (not to be confused with a degree in <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">civil engineering</a>, which is but one of many degrees linked to the title <i>sivilingeniør</i>, which is still in use for new graduates who can choose to also use the old title). All pre-2001 doctoral degree titles were replaced with the title "Philosophical Doctor degree", written <i>philosophiæ doctor</i> (instead of the traditional <i>doctor philosophiæ</i>). The title <a href="/wiki/Dr._philos._(Norwegian_degree)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dr. philos. (Norwegian degree)">dr. philos.</a> is a substantially higher degree than the PhD<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and is reserved for those who qualify for such a degree without participating in an organized doctoral degree program.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> the system is similar to the German one.
</p>
<ul><li><i><i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">licencjat</i></i> title – given by a <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">university</a>; the equivalent of <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">Bachelor of Arts</a> degree or <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">Bachelor of Science</a> degree (depending on <a href="/wiki/Academic_major" class="mw-redirect" title="Academic major">academic major</a>); granted after at least 3 years of study.</li>
<li><i><i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">inżynier</i></i> (<i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">inż.</i>) title – <a href="/wiki/Engineer%27s_degree#Poland,_Czech_Republic_and_Slovakia" title="Engineer&#39;s degree">Engineer's degree</a> given by a <a href="/wiki/Technical_university" class="mw-redirect" title="Technical university">technical university</a>; granted after at least about 4 years of study.</li>
<li><i><i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">magister</i></i> (<i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">mgr</i>) title – the equivalent of a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Arts" title="Master of Arts">Master of Arts</a> or <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Science" title="Master of Science">Master of Science</a> degree, granted after 5–6 years of study or 2 years of additional study by holders of a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor degree">bachelor degree</a> with classification of <a href="/wiki/Honours_Degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Honours Degree">Honours Degree</a>.</li>
<li><i><i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">magister inżynier</i></i> (<i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">mgr inż.</i>) title – the equivalent of a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Engineering" title="Master of Engineering">Master of Engineering</a>, granted after about 2 years of additional study by holders of a degree of <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Engineering" title="Bachelor of Engineering">Bachelor of Engineering</a>.</li>
<li><i><i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">doktor</i></i> (<i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">dr</i>) degree – the equivalent of <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">Doctor of Philosophy</a>.</li>
<li><i><i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">doktor habilitowany</i></i> (<i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">dr hab.</i>) degree – Polish <a href="/wiki/Habilitation" title="Habilitation">Habilitation</a> degree, requires approval by an external ministerial body.</li>
<li><i><i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">profesor</i></i> (<i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">prof.</i>) degree – the highest title, officially conferred by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Poland" title="President of Poland">President of Poland</a>.</li></ul>
<h4><span id="Russia.2C_Ukraine_and_some_other_former_USSR_republics"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia,_Ukraine_and_some_other_former_USSR_republics">Russia, Ukraine and some other former USSR republics<span id="Russia"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Russia, Ukraine and some other former USSR republics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2010</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Since 1992, Russian higher education has introduced a multilevel system, enabling higher education institutions to award and issue Bachelor of Science and Master of Science Degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> and some other <a href="/wiki/Former_USSR_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Former USSR republic">former USSR republics</a> educational degrees are awarded after finishing college education. There are several levels of education one must choose between 2nd and 3rd year usually on the 3rd year of study.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">Bachelor degree</a> – usually takes 4 years of college. (minimum level to be recognized as having Higher Education)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Specialist_degree" title="Specialist degree">Specialist degree</a> is awarded after 5 years of college. (4 + 1)</li>
<li>Master's (Magister) degree is awarded after 6 years of college. (4 + 2)<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></li></ol>
<p>(But Specialist degree can appear equivalent to Magister degree by reason of equivalence of amount of educational time).
Usually Specialist or Magister degrees incorporates bachelor's degree in them, but only high-level degree is stated in final diploma.
Specialist and Magister degrees require taking final state exams and written work on practical application of studied skills
or research thesis (usually 70-100 pages) and is roughly equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master&#39;s degree">Master's degree</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guidelines_for_the_recognition_of_Russian_qualifications_in_the_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guidelines_for_the_recognition_of_Russian_qualifications_in_the-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first level academic degree is called "<a href="/wiki/Kandidat_nauk" class="mw-redirect" title="Kandidat nauk">Kandidat nauk</a>" (that could be translated verbatim as a "Candidate of Sciences"). This degree requires extensive research efforts, taking some classes, publications in peer-reviewed academic journals (not less than 5 publications in Ukraine or 3 publications in Russia), taking 3 or more exams (one or more in their speciality, one in a foreign language and one in the history and philosophy of science) and writing and defending an in-depth thesis (80-200 pages) called a "dissertation".
</p><p>Finally, there is a "<a href="/wiki/Doktor_nauk" title="Doktor nauk">Doktor Nauk</a>" (that could be translated verbatim as a "Doctor of Sciences") degree in Russia and some former USSR academic environment. This degree is granted for contributions in a certain field (formally – who established new direction or new field in science). It requires discovery of new phenomenon or development of new theory or essential development of new direction, etc. There is no equivalent of this "doctor of sciences" degree in US academic system. It is roughly equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Habilitation" title="Habilitation">Habilitation</a> in Germany, France, Austria and some other European countries.
</p><p>In countries with a two-tier system of doctoral degrees, the degree of <i>Kandidat Nauk</i> should be considered for recognition at the level of the first doctoral degree. In countries with only one doctoral degree, the degree of Kandidat Nauk should be considered for recognition as equivalent to this degree.
</p><p>According to <i>Guidelines for the recognition of Russian qualifications in the other countries</i><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> In countries with a two-tier system of doctoral degrees, the degree of <i>Doktor Nauk</i> should be considered for recognition at the level of the second doctoral degree. In countries in which only one doctoral degree exists, the degree of Doktor Nauk should be considered for recognition at the level of this degree.
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Classification_of_Education" title="International Standard Classification of Education">International Standard Classification of Education</a> (ISCED) UNESCO 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> par.262 for purposes of international educational statistics
</p>
<ol><li>DPhil to <i>Kandidat Nauk/Philosophy</i>,</li>
<li>D.Lit to <i>Kandidat Nauk in Literature</i>,</li>
<li>D.Sc to <i>Kandidat Nauk of Natural Science</i>,</li>
<li>LL.D to <i>Kandidat Nauk of Legal Science</i>.</li></ol>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Spain's higher-education legal framework includes: Official and accredited education and Non-official education.
</p><p><b>1.1 Official and accredited education.</b>
</p><p>In Spain, accreditation of official university study programmes is regulated by law and monitored by governmental agencies responsible for verifying their quality and suitability for official approval and accreditation.
</p><p>Official professional study programmes lead to degree qualifications (<i>Títulos</i>) with full academic and professional effects and the degrees awarded in accordance with the latest higher-education system are:
</p><p>1. Bachelor’s Degree (<i>Grado</i>) – 240 ECTS Credits in 4 years.
</p><p>2. Master’s Degree (<i>Master Universitario</i>) – 60 to 120 ECTS Credits in 1–2 years.
</p><p>3. Doctoral degree PhD (<i>Doctorado</i>) – in 3–4 years.
</p><p>Accredited bachelor's degrees and master's degrees qualifications will always be described as "<i>Grado</i>" and "<i>Master Universitario</i>". These qualifications comply with the European Higher Education Area (EHEA)<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> framework. Officially approved and accredited university study programmes must implement this framework by law in order to attain and retain accreditation in Spain.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_02.jpg/220px-Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_02.jpg/330px-Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_02.jpg/440px-Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1276" data-file-height="955" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish Official University Education Legal Framework 02</div></div></div>
<p><b>1.2 Non-official education.</b>
</p><p>Not all EHEA compliant study programmes in Spain are officially approved and/or accredited by government agencies. Some universities offer proprietary study programmes as an alternative to accredited study programmes for a variety of reasons: attending the continuing education market for individual self-advancement and also providing higher education to individuals that have failed to acquire bachelor's degree qualifications. The main reason for offering this alternative studies, though, is the heavy bureaucratic process that needs to be accomplished to receive the approval of specific titles, in particular when it refers to new studies or studies about matters that do not fit with the official studies. For historical reasons, the academic system has been very much under the control of the State and private universities are still regarded with as a threat to the State system.
</p><p>These programmes fall within the category of "Non officially approved and accredited" or "<i>Estudios no oficiales</i>" and they have no academic or professional effects. This means that they do not entitle the bearer to claim to have any specific academic or professional qualifications, as far as the Spanish authorities are concerned. However, there may be private agreements to recognize the titles.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_01.jpg/220px-Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_01.jpg/330px-Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_01.jpg/440px-Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1269" data-file-height="931" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spanish_Official_University_Education_Legal_Framework_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish Official University Education Legal Framework 01</div></div></div>
<p>Universities offering non-official study programmes are legally bound to clearly differentiate between officially approved and non-officially approved qualifications when naming their offer of non-official qualifications. Non-accredited master's degrees will be described as "<i>Master</i>" on its own, without the term "<i>Universitario</i>".
</p><p>Certain non-officially approved and accredited study programmes may acquire a well deserved reputation. However, neither Professional Association, Government Agencies, Judiciary Authorities, nor Universities -other than the study programme provider- are obliged to recognize non-official qualifications in any way.
</p><p><b>2. Accreditation System</b>
</p><p>University taught study programmes accreditation is granted through the ANECA,<sup id="cite_ref-aneca.es_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aneca.es-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> a government dependent quality assurance and accreditation provider for the Spanish Higher Education System and ensures that the data held in the RUCT,<sup id="cite_ref-educacion.gob.es_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-educacion.gob.es-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> a national registry for universities and qualifications, is correct and up to date. All study programmes must be accredited by ANECA<sup id="cite_ref-aneca.es_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aneca.es-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> prior to their inclusion in the RUCT.<sup id="cite_ref-educacion.gob.es_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-educacion.gob.es-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
The RUCT<sup id="cite_ref-educacion.gob.es_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-educacion.gob.es-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> records all officially approved Universities and their bachelor's degrees, Master's Degrees and PhDs and each and every one of the officially approved and accredited study programmes and universities are assigned a specific number Code (<i>Código</i>) by the RUCT. The same study programme may acquire different codes as it progresses through various stages of official approval by local government and central government.
</p><p>Prospective students should check the RUCT<sup id="cite_ref-educacion.gob.es_92-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-educacion.gob.es-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Code awarded to the study programme of their interest at every stage of their enquiries concerning degrees in Spain.
</p><p>ANECA makes recommendations regarding procedures, staffing levels, quality of teaching, resources available to students and continuity or loss of accreditation and the ANECA Registry<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> records all events in the life of an officially approved and accredited study programme or a university. The ANECA Registry Search Facility<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> may be the simplest and safest way to verify the status of all officially approved and accredited study programmes in Spain.
</p><p>It is also possible to track qualifications by using the search facility that several Autonomous Communities own accreditation agencies offer. These agencies work within the ANECA framework and generally show more detailed information about the study programmes available in each territory (i.e.: Catalonia, Madrid, etc.)
</p><p><b>3. Qualifications framework for Higher Education.</b>
</p><p>The qualifications framework for higher education <a href="/wiki/QF-EHEA" title="QF-EHEA">MECES</a> is the reference framework adopted in Spain in order to structure degree levels.
</p><p>Not all universities offer degrees named exactly the same, even if they have similar academic and professional effects. Each university may present proposals for the study programme considered to meet professional and academic demand. The proposal will consist of a report linking the study programme being considered and the proposed qualification to be awarded. This report will be assessed by ANECA and sent for the Consejo de Universidades Españolas.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> If the <i>Consejo</i> agrees with ANECA’s approval, it will be included in the RUCT and ANECA registries.
<b></b>
4. Spanish qualifications and their professional effects.<b></b>
</p><p>All bachelor's and master's degrees accredited by ANECA enjoy full academic and professional effects in accordance with new and previous laws. Professional practice law in Spain is currently under revision.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sweden">Sweden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Sweden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bologna_process#Sweden" class="mw-redirect" title="Bologna process">Bologna process §&#160;Sweden</a></div>
<table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2008</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Switzerland">Switzerland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Switzerland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Before the <a href="/wiki/Bologna_Process" title="Bologna Process">Bologna Process</a> after 4 or 5 years of study the academic degree of a <a href="/wiki/Licentiate_(degree)" title="Licentiate (degree)">Licentiate</a> was reached.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Depending on the official language of the university it was called <i>Lizentiat</i> (German) <i>Licence</i> (French) or <i>licenza</i> (Italian) and is today considered equivalent<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> to the <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master&#39;s degree">Master's degree</a> according to the Bologna reform. A Licentiate with a predefined qualification gave access to the last stage of further two or more years of studies (depending on the field) for a <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">Doctoral's degree</a>.
</p><p>Apart from this most universities offered a <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_Diploma" class="mw-redirect" title="Postgraduate Diploma">Postgraduate Diploma</a> with up to two years of study. French-speaking universities called them <i>diplôme d'études approfondies</i> <a href="/wiki/DEA_(former_French_degree)" class="mw-redirect" title="DEA (former French degree)">DEA or DESS</a>, the Italian-speaking University <i>post laurea</i> and German-speaking universities mostly <i>Nachdiplomstudium</i> (NDS). Today the federal legislation defines these postgraduate diplomas (60 ECTS credits) as <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Advanced_Studies" title="Master of Advanced Studies">Master of Advanced Studies</a> (MAS) or Executive Master of Business Administration (EMBA) degree. Universities may also offer the possibility to gain a Diploma of Advanced Studies (DAS), less than 60 ECTS credits).<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> These degrees do not normally give access to the doctorate study.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span id="England.2C_Wales_and_Northern_Ireland"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="England,_Wales_and_Northern_Ireland">England, Wales and Northern Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: England, Wales and Northern Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:King%27s_College_London_Medical_School_Graduates.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/King%27s_College_London_Medical_School_Graduates.png/250px-King%27s_College_London_Medical_School_Graduates.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/King%27s_College_London_Medical_School_Graduates.png/375px-King%27s_College_London_Medical_School_Graduates.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/King%27s_College_London_Medical_School_Graduates.png/500px-King%27s_College_London_Medical_School_Graduates.png 2x" data-file-width="1334" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:King%27s_College_London_Medical_School_Graduates.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The newly conferred bachelor's degree holders after graduation at <a href="/wiki/King%27s_College_London" title="King&#39;s College London">King's College London</a>, one of the founding colleges of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a></div></div></div>
<p>The title 'degree' is protected under UK law. All valid UK degrees are awarded by universities or other degree-awarding bodies whose powers to do so are recognised by the UK government; hence they are known as 'recognised bodies'.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The standard <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_degree" title="Undergraduate degree">first degree</a> in England, Northern Ireland and Wales is the <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">Bachelor's degree</a> conferred with honours. Usually this is a Bachelor of Arts (BA) or Bachelor of Science (BSc) degree. Other variants exist, for example Bachelor of Education. It usually takes three years to read for a bachelor's degree.
</p><p>The honours are usually categorised into four classes:
</p>
<ul><li>First class honours (1st)</li>
<li>Second class honours, divided into:
<ul><li>Upper division or upper second (2:1)</li>
<li>Lower division or lower second (2:2)</li></ul></li>
<li>Third class honours (3rd)</li></ul>
<p>Candidates who have not achieved the standard for the award of honours may be admitted without honours to the 'ordinary' Bachelor's degree if they have met the required standard for this lesser qualification (also referred to as a 'pass degree'). Standard levels for each of these classes are 70%+ for a first, 60-69% for a 2:1, 50-59% for a 2:2, 40-49% for a 3rd and 30%+ for a pass degree, although this can vary by institution (e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Open_University" title="Open University">Open University</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Foundation_degree" title="Foundation degree">foundation degree</a><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> is a qualification at lower than Bachelor's level awarded following a two-year programme of study that is usually vocational in nature. The foundation degree can be awarded by a university or college of higher education that has been granted foundation degree awarding powers by the UK government. This degree is comparable to an <a href="/wiki/Associate_degree" title="Associate degree">associate degree</a> in the United States.
</p><p>The universities of Oxford and Cambridge award honorary Master of Arts (MA) degrees to graduates of their Bachelor's programmes, following a specified period of time. This is comparable to the practice of the ancient universities in Scotland of awarding an MA for a first degree and arguably reflects the rigorous standards expected of their graduates.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degrees" class="mw-redirect" title="Master&#39;s degrees">Master's degrees</a><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> such as Master of Arts or Master of Science are typically awarded to students who have undertaken at least a year of full-time <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">postgraduate study</a>, which may be taught or, in many cases, involve an element of research. Degrees such as Master of Philosophy (MPhil) or Master of Letters/Literature (MLitt) are likely to be awarded for postgraduate degrees involving original research. A student undertaking a Master's would normally be expected to already hold an honours degree in a relevant subject, hence the possibility of reaching Master's level in one year.
</p><p>Some universities award a Master's as a first degree following an integrated programme of study (an 'integrated master's degree'). These degrees are usually designated by the subject, such as <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Engineering" title="Master of Engineering">Master of Engineering</a> for engineering, <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Physics" title="Master of Physics">Master of Physics</a> for physics, <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Mathematics" title="Master of Mathematics">Master of Mathematics</a> for mathematics and so on; it usually takes four years to read for them. Graduation to these degrees is always with honours. Master of Engineering in particular has now become the standard first degree in engineering at the top UK universities, replacing the older Bachelor of Engineering.
</p><p>The Master of Business Administration (MBA) degree is highly valued by those seeking to advance in business as managers and decision makers.
</p><p>Doctoral degrees or <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctorates</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> such as the Doctor of Philosophy degree (PhD or DPhil) or Doctor of Education (EdD or DEd) are awarded following a programme of original research that contributes new knowledge within the context of the student's discipline. Doctoral degrees usually take three years full-time. Therefore, in the UK it may only take seven years to progress from undergraduate to doctoral level – in some cases six, since having a Master's is not always a precondition for embarking on a doctoral degree. This contrasts with nine years in the United States, reflecting differences in the educational systems.
</p><p>Some doctorates, such as the Doctor of Clinical Psychology (DClinPsy) qualification, confirm competence to practice in particular professions. There are also higher doctorates – Doctor of Science (DSc) and Doctor of Letters/Literature (DLitt) that are typically awarded to experienced academics who have demonstrated a high level of achievement in their academic career; for example they may have published widely on their subject or become professors in their field.
</p><p>UK post-secondary qualifications are defined at different levels, with levels 1-3 denoting further education and levels 4-8 denoting higher education. Within this structure, a foundation degree is at level 5; a Bachelor's at level 6; at Master's at level 7; and a doctoral degree at level 8.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
Full information about the expectations for different types of UK degree is published by the <a href="/wiki/Quality_Assurance_Agency_for_Higher_Education" title="Quality Assurance Agency for Higher Education">Quality Assurance Agency for Higher Education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>See also <a href="/wiki/Graduate_certificate" title="Graduate certificate">graduate certificate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graduate_diploma" title="Graduate diploma">graduate diploma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_certificate" title="Postgraduate certificate">postgraduate certificate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_diploma" title="Postgraduate diploma">postgraduate diploma</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_degree_abbreviations" title="British degree abbreviations">British degree abbreviations</a>.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Scotland">Scotland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Scotland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The standard <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_degree" title="Undergraduate degree">first degree</a> for students studying arts or humanities in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> is either a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">Bachelor of Arts</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Arts_(Scotland)" title="Master of Arts (Scotland)">Master of Arts</a> (the latter traditionally awarded by the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Universities_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Universities of Scotland">Ancient Universities of Scotland</a> for a first degree in an arts/humanities subject). The standard undergraduate degree for natural and social science subjects is the <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">Bachelor of Science</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Students can work towards a first degree at either ordinary or honours level. A general or ordinary degree (BA/MA or BSc) takes three years to complete; an honours degree (BA/MA Hons or BSc Hons) takes four years. The ordinary degree need not be in a specific subject, but can involve study across a range of subjects within (and sometimes beyond) the relevant faculty, in which case it may also be called a general degree; if a third year or junior honours subject is included, the ordinary degree in that named discipline is awarded. The honours degree involves two years of study at a sub-honours level in which a range of subjects within the relevant faculty are studied and then two years of study at honours level which is specialised in a single field (for example classics, history, chemistry, biology, etc.).Not all Universities in Scotland adhere to this, in some you study in several subjects within a faculty for three years and can then specialise in two areas and attain a joint honours degree in fourth year.
</p><p>This also reflects the broader scope of the final years of <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Scotland" title="Education in Scotland">Scottish secondary education</a>, where traditionally five <a href="/wiki/Higher_(Scottish)" title="Higher (Scottish)">Highers</a> are studied, compared to (typically) three English or Welsh <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Level_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced Level (UK)">A-Levels</a>. The Higher is a one-year qualification, as opposed to the two years of A-Levels, which accounts for Scottish honours degrees being a year longer than those in England. <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Higher_(Scottish)" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced Higher (Scottish)">Advanced Highers</a> add an optional final year of secondary education, bringing students up to the level of their A-Level counterparts – students with strong A-Levels or Advanced Highers may be offered entry directly into the second year at Scottish universities.
</p><p>Honours for MA or bachelor's degrees are classified into three classes:
</p>
<ul><li>First class honours</li>
<li>Second class honours, divided into:
<ul><li>Division one (2:1) [Upper Second Class Honours]</li>
<li>Division two (2:2) [Lower Second Class Honours]</li></ul></li>
<li>Third class honours</li></ul>
<p>Students who complete all the requirements for an honours degree, but do not receive sufficient merit to be awarded third-class honours may be awarded a <i>Special Degree</i> (ordinary degree – bachelor's level SCQF Level 9).
</p><p>In most respects, the criteria for awarding qualifications at honours level and above are the same as in the rest of the UK (see above under England, Wales and Northern Ireland). Postgraduate qualifications are not designated Master of Arts as in the rest of the UK, as this is an undergraduate degree. Postgraduate degrees in arts and humanities subjects are usually designated <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Letters" title="Master of Letters">Master of Letters</a> (M.Litt) or, in natural and social sciences, <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Science" title="Master of Science">Master of Science</a> (M.Sc). Non-doctoral postgraduate research degrees are usually designated <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Philosophy" title="Master of Philosophy">Master of Philosophy</a> (M.Phil) or <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Research" title="Master of Research">Master of Research</a> (M.Res). The postgraduate teaching qualification is the postgraduate diploma in Education (PGDE).
</p><p>Postgraduate qualifications are classified into four classes:
</p>
<ul><li>Distinction</li>
<li>Credit</li>
<li>Merit</li>
<li>Pass</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Canada, education is the responsibility of the provinces and territories, rather than the federal government. However, all of Canada follows the three level bachelor's—master's—doctorate system common to the Anglophone world, with a few variations. A common framework for degrees was agreed between the provinces and territories in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_Framework_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada_Framework-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bachelor's degrees are normally three to four years in duration, although more commonly three years in Quebec (where they follow on from college courses rather than directly from secondary education). Master's degrees take one to three years, again with the exception of Quebec where they take one and a half to two years and doctorates take a minimum of three years. Alone among Canadian provinces and territories, British Columbia offers two year <a href="/wiki/Associate_degree" title="Associate degree">associate degrees</a>, allowing credit to be transferred into a four-year bachelor's program.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Three year bachelor's degrees are normally ordinary degrees, while four year degrees are <a href="/wiki/Honours_degree" title="Honours degree">honours degrees</a>; an honours degree is normally needed for further study at master's level.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Canada, <a href="/wiki/First_professional_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="First professional degree">first professional degrees</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Dental_Surgery" class="mw-redirect" title="Doctor of Dental Surgery">DDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">MD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Pharmacy" title="Doctor of Pharmacy">PharmD</a> and <a href="/wiki/LLB" class="mw-redirect" title="LLB">LLB</a> or <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">JD</a> are considered bachelor's level qualifications, despite their often being named as if they were doctorates.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_Framework_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada_Framework-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Quebec">Quebec</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Quebec">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>In the province of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, the majority of students must attend <a href="/wiki/College_education_in_Quebec" title="College education in Quebec">college</a> prior to entering university. Upon completion of a two-year pre-university program, such as in Sciences or Humanities or a three-year technical program, such as Nursing or Computer Science, college graduates obtain a <i><a href="/wiki/Quebec_College_Diploma" title="Quebec College Diploma">college diploma</a></i>, which is a prerequisite access for university-level studies. Although the previously mentioned college programs are typical, they are <i>not</i> offered in every institution in the province. Moreover, while a few other pre-university programs with various concentrations exist, many other technical/career programs are available depending on the college of choice. For example, <a href="/wiki/Dawson_College" title="Dawson College">Dawson College</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> has nearly sixty different programs leading to a college diploma. Special programs, such as <a href="/wiki/Physical_rehabilitation" class="mw-redirect" title="Physical rehabilitation">physical rehabilitation therapy</a>, are offered in some colleges as well. These programs are particularly interesting because they allow students to enter professional university programs, such as <a href="/wiki/Physiotherapy" class="mw-redirect" title="Physiotherapy">physiotherapy</a> (which consists of an integrated <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science_in_Physiotherapy" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor of Science in Physiotherapy">Bachelor of Science in Physiotherapy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Physical_Therapy" title="Master of Physical Therapy">Master of Physical Therapy</a>), without having to meet the usual grade and course prerequisites required from students holding a pre-university science diploma. A similar option is offered for college nursing graduates as they can pursue their studies in university to obtain a <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Nursing" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor of Nursing">Bachelor of Nursing</a> in two years (rather than the usual three or four years, depending on whether the student has completed a college diploma in Quebec). Additionally, whereas aspiring medical students are usually required to complete an <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_degree" title="Undergraduate degree">undergraduate degree</a> before applying to medical schools, Quebec college graduates have the option to enter:
</p>
<ul><li>a "medical preparatory" year at <a href="/wiki/McGill_University" title="McGill University">McGill University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_de_Montr%C3%A9al" title="Université de Montréal">Université de Montréal</a> and then pursue medical studies for the four following years or</li>
<li>simply directly into the undergraduate medical education program at <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Laval" title="Université Laval">Université Laval</a> (4 to 5 years in duration) or <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_de_Sherbrooke" title="Université de Sherbrooke">Université de Sherbrooke</a> (4 years in duration).</li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mexico">Mexico</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Mexico">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Education in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> follows a three-degree system similar to that of Canada and the US. The pre-university academic level is the <i>bachillerato</i> (also called <i>preparatoria</i>), similar to <a href="/wiki/High_school_(upper_secondary)" class="mw-redirect" title="High school (upper secondary)">high school</a>. Students typically leave preparatoria at the age of 18 for university, at which point they choose to specialize in a specific academic area (a <i>carrera</i>).
</p><p>After high school, students progress to university, where they study for a <i>Técnico Superior universitario</i> (Associate degree)<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> or a <i>licenciatura</i> (Bachelor), then a <i>maestría</i> (Master), then a <i>doctorado</i>(doctorate).
</p><p>Once in university, students begin the <i>carrera</i>, the study of a precise academic branch like economics, business administration, sciences, law, engineering or medicine. Students will be in university for 8-10 semesters of full-time study, which typically takes 4–5 years. Upon graduation, students receive a <i>licenciatura</i>  in their chosen subject area, which is equivalent to an American <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">Bachelor's degree</a>. They can also get the degree of "ingenieria" or "medico" that refers to an engineer or MD respectively.
</p><p>Several Mexican universities offer students the possibility of obtaining an equivalent to an <a href="/wiki/Associate_degree" title="Associate degree">Associate degree</a>, called in Mexico <i>Técnico Superior universitario</i> (TSU), studying only half of the <i>licenciatura</i>, with the possibility of finishing a full bachelor's degree later.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> This is done mainly in fields like engineering and computer sciences.
</p><p>After receiving the <i>licenciatura</i>, students may take extra courses called <i>diplomados</i> (similar to a <a href="/wiki/Certification" title="Certification">Certification</a> but issued by a university). These courses last 4–12 months and are a means to further study without continuing to the next degree level, usually studied to demonstrate that the student still updated in his field. Most students stay at this level, but some choose to continue to the <i>maestría</i>, equivalent to the <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master&#39;s degree">Master's degree</a>. Study at the <i>maestría</i> level takes 1–3 years and mandates completion of a <a href="/wiki/Thesis" title="Thesis">thesis</a>. Post-graduate students in Mexico typically enter a master's program after a few years in the workforce and often continue working while studying.
</p><p>Traditionally, students who have completed the <i>maestria</i> may continue on to the <i>doctorado</i> or the <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctorate</a>. Doctoral study typically lasts 3–4 years. In last years this schemes has become flexible such that in some PhD programmes, students are accepted before or not completing at all a Master course.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In the United States, since the late 19th century, the threefold degree system of bachelor, master and doctor has been in place, but has evolved into a slightly different pattern from the European equivalent. The <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Education" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Department of Education">U.S. Department of Education</a> now classifies degrees in six categories: <a href="/wiki/Associate_degree" title="Associate degree">associate degrees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">bachelor's degrees</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_professional_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="First professional degree">first professional degrees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degrees" class="mw-redirect" title="Master&#39;s degrees">master's degrees</a>, intermediate graduate qualifications and <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">research doctorates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The standard academic progression remains bachelor's—master's—(research) doctorate. Most standard <i>academic</i> programs are based on the four-year bachelor's degree, most often <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Arts" title="Bachelor of Arts">Bachelor of Arts</a> (B.A.) or <a href="/wiki/Bachelor_of_Science" title="Bachelor of Science">Bachelor of Science</a> (B.S.), a one- or two-year master's degree (most often <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Arts" title="Master of Arts">Master of Arts</a> (M.A.) or <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Science" title="Master of Science">Master of Science</a> (M.S.); either of these programs might be as long as three years in length) and a further two to five years of coursework and research, culminating in "comprehensive" examinations in one or more fields, plus perhaps some teaching experience and then the writing of a dissertation for the doctorate, for a total of ten or more years from starting the bachelor's degree (which is usually begun around age 18) to the awarding of the doctorate. This timetable is only approximate, however, as students in accelerated programs can sometimes earn a bachelor's degree in three years or, on the other hand, a particular dissertation project might take four or more years to complete. In addition, a graduate may wait an indeterminate time between degrees before candidacy in the next level or even an additional degree at a level already completed. Therefore, there is no time-limit on the accumulation of academic degrees.
</p><p>By far the most common research doctorate is the <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Philosophy" title="Doctor of Philosophy">Doctor of Philosophy</a> (Ph.D.), comprising  98.1% of research doctorates in 2014. The  <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Education" title="Doctor of Education">Doctor of Education</a> (Ed.D.) made up 1.1% (not including Ed.D.s classified as professional degrees rather than research doctorates) and all other research doctorates were less than 1% in total.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some schools, mostly <a href="/wiki/Junior_college" title="Junior college">junior colleges</a> and <a href="/wiki/Community_college" title="Community college">community colleges</a> and some four-year schools, offer an <a href="/wiki/Associate_degree" title="Associate degree">associate degree</a> for two full years of study. These may be in professional or academic fields and the most common awards are the Associate of Arts (A.A.) and Associate of Science (A.S.) degrees. <a href="/wiki/Articulation_(education)" title="Articulation (education)">Articulation</a> agreements may allow credit earned on an associate degree to be counted toward completion of a bachelor's degree.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The "<a href="/wiki/First_professional_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="First professional degree">first professional degree</a>" is a graduate level degree program designed to prepare graduates for professional practice in various fields other than academic scholarship and research.  First professional degrees require a minimum of two years prior college-level education to enter the program and a minimum of six years total college-level education (including that undertaken prior to entry) to complete the program.<sup id="cite_ref-US_Department_of_Education_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_Department_of_Education-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Most professional degree programs require a prior bachelor's degree for admission and many require seven or eight years of total study. Many first professional degrees, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">M.D.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">J.D.</a> or <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Osteopathic_Medicine" title="Doctor of Osteopathic Medicine">D.O.</a> are named as doctorates but should not be confused with research doctorates such as the Ph.D.<sup id="cite_ref-US_Department_of_Education_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US_Department_of_Education-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> First professional degrees should also not be confused with professional master's degrees such as the <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Architecture" title="Master of Architecture">M.Arch.</a> and <a href="/wiki/M.B.A." class="mw-redirect" title="M.B.A.">M.B.A.</a>, which are classified as master's degrees,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> or with intermediate graduate qualifications that also bear the title of doctor, such as <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Ministry" title="Doctor of Ministry">D.Min.</a> or <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Psychology" title="Doctor of Psychology">D.Psy.</a><sup id="cite_ref-Intermediate_Graduate_Qualifications_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intermediate_Graduate_Qualifications-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Intermediate graduate qualifications lie between master's level and the doctorate. They include awards such as Advanced Certificates, Advanced Graduate Certificates, <a href="/wiki/Graduate_Diploma" class="mw-redirect" title="Graduate Diploma">Graduate Diplomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Professional_Engineer" class="mw-redirect" title="Professional Engineer">Professional Engineer</a> status and Professional Diplomas, as well as <a href="/wiki/Specialist_degree" title="Specialist degree">specialist degrees</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Education_Specialist" class="mw-redirect" title="Education Specialist">Education Specialist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Ministry" title="Doctor of Ministry">Doctor of Ministry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Psychology" title="Doctor of Psychology">Doctor of Psychology</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Licentiate_in_Sacred_Theology" class="mw-redirect" title="Licentiate in Sacred Theology">Licentiate in Sacred Theology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Intermediate_Graduate_Qualifications_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Intermediate_Graduate_Qualifications-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 21 US jurisdictions, religious institutions can be authorized to grant religious-exempt (rel. exmpt., rel. expt. etc.) degrees without accreditation or government oversight.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> Such degrees are used primarily to attain church-related employment.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_levels_of_attainment_of_degrees">Current levels of attainment of degrees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Current levels of attainment of degrees">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Traditionally more men than women attended and earned degrees at the world's universities. A milestone was reached in the United States according to results of the 2010 census, as women surpassed men in attaining master's degrees, for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The U.S. census reports that 10.5 million men have master's degrees or higher, compared with 10.6 million women. The first year that women surpassed men in earning bachelor's degrees was in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Perceptions_of_the_value_of_a_degree_in_the_US">Perceptions of the value of a degree in the US</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Perceptions of the value of a degree in the US">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Students, the media and the general public have shown much concern over the value of getting a higher degree in the US ever since the Great Recession of 2007. A 2015 survey of 2,000 adults (900 of which were graduates), implemented by an education technology company called Greenwood Hall, reported that more than half of the graduates surveyed believe those getting their degree now will be receiving a lower return on their investment than their counterparts 10–15 years ago.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Media coverage of the rising costs of higher education and increased student debt have also affected the public’s perceptions of whether higher degrees are still worthwhile. Statistics citing that college graduates make around $1 million more in their lifetimes than those who didn’t attend college and living longer, healthier lives work in favor of those who argue the continued value of higher degrees.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Studies like the 2011 Learning Gains study by Arum and Roksa, on the other hand, reported that only 55% of students had any learning gains during their first two years of college, which favors the argument that investing in higher education may not still be worth it.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> As academics continue researching and dissecting these arguments, education remains a hot topic in the US as shown by President Obama recently setting a national goal for the US to once again have the highest proportion of college graduates in the world by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Australian_Qualifications_Framework" title="Australian Qualifications Framework">Australian Qualifications Framework</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Qualifications_Framework" title="Australian Qualifications Framework">Australian Qualifications Framework</a> (AQF) covers 10 levels, of which 6 – 10 correspond to academic degrees. These are the <i><a href="/wiki/Associate_degree" title="Associate degree">associate degree</a></i> (level 6), which normally takes 2 years, the <i><a href="/wiki/Bachelor_degree" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachelor degree">bachelor degree</a></i> (level 7), which normally takes 3 years, the <i><a href="/wiki/Honours_degree" title="Honours degree">bachelor honours degree</a></i> (level 8), which normally takes 1 year after the bachelor degree and is mostly taken as an optional extension year depending of the discipline, the <i>master degree</i>  (level 9), which normally takes 1 – 2 years for "research" or "coursework" degrees and 3 – 4 years for an "extended" degree and follows on from either a bachelor or honours degree and the <i><a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctoral degree</a></i> (level 10), which normally takes 3 – 4 years following on from a master's degree or a Class I or IIa honours qualification. Also included within the higher education system are <a href="/wiki/Graduate_certificate" title="Graduate certificate">graduate certificates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Graduate_diploma" title="Graduate diploma">graduate diplomas</a>, both of which are at level 8 (honours degree level), as well as advanced diplomas, at level 6 (associate degree level) and diplomas at level 5 (first year of a degree course).<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AQF_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AQF-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In Australia, most degrees are issued ungraded, with bachelor's degrees with honours being the exception.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Doctorates in Australia may be research doctorates (normally titled <a href="/wiki/PhD" class="mw-redirect" title="PhD">PhDs</a>) or professional doctorates (normally titled to refer to the field of practice, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Engineering" title="Doctor of Engineering">Doctor of Engineering</a>. Professional doctorates still require research leading to "a significant and original contribution to knowledge in the context of professional practice" and should not be confused with extended master's degrees that bear similar names for historical reasons: the <a href="/wiki/Juris_Doctor" title="Juris Doctor">Juris Doctor</a> and Doctors of Medical Practice, Physiotherapy, Dentistry and Optometry. Despite their names, these extended master's degrees may not be described as doctoral degrees nor do they confer the right to use the title of doctor on their recipients.<sup id="cite_ref-AQF_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AQF-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some bachelor's degrees (e.g. Bachelor of Engineering or Bachelor of Medicine/Bachelor of Surgery) may take longer than three years to complete and double bachelor's degrees (i.e. completing two bachelor's degrees simultaneously in four to five years) are common.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_education_in_New_Zealand" title="Tertiary education in New Zealand">Tertiary education in New Zealand</a></div>
<p>Like Australia, New Zealand has a 10-level qualifications framework (the New Zealand Qualifications Framework; NZQF) and a referencing exercise has found a one-to-one correspondence between the levels of the two frameworks.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> However, the names given to qualifications at different levels are not the same and New Zealand does not have associate degrees, thus only levels 7 – 10 correspond to academic degrees. These are the <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">bachelor's degree</a> (level 7), <a href="/wiki/Honours_degree" title="Honours degree">bachelor honours degree</a> (level 8), <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master&#39;s degree">master's degree</a> (level 9) and the <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctoral degree</a> (level 10).
