In addition to these, the NZQF has certificates across levels 1 – 6, diplomas at levels 5 and 6, <a href="/wiki/Graduate_certificate" title="Graduate certificate">graduate certificates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Graduate_diploma" title="Graduate diploma">graduate diplomas</a> at level 7 (bachelor's) and <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_certificate" title="Postgraduate certificate">postgraduate certificates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_diploma" title="Postgraduate diploma">postgraduate diplomas</a> at level 8 (honours).<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Another referencing exercise, comparing the NZQF to the 10-level Irish National Framework for Qualifications found that degrees were comparable but that further work was needed to improve compatibility for the sub-degree levels (1 – 6). Non-degree qualifications at levels 7 – 9 were not included in the study.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In New Zealand, master's degrees may be awarded with classified honours (1st, 2:1, 2:2, 3rd) or with distinction or merit.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Argentina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Argentina" title="Education in Argentina">Education in Argentina</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Undergraduate students in Brazilian universities graduate either with a bachelor's degree, a Licentiate degree or a Technologist degree.
</p><p>Bachelor degrees in Brazil normally takes four or five years of full-time study to complete, with the exception of the human medicine course which requires six years.
</p><p>Licentiate degree, normally takes four-years length degrees, available for students who want to qualify as <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">school</a> teachers. <i>Licenciatura</i> courses exist mostly in mathematics, humanities and natural sciences.
</p><p>Technologist degree is available in technology-related fields and can be normally obtained in three years. These degrees are turned to fast entry the industry.
</p><p>Admission as an undergraduate student in most top public or private universities in Brazil requires that the applicant pass a competitive entrance examination known as <a href="/wiki/Vestibular" class="mw-redirect" title="Vestibular">Vestibular</a>. Contrary to what happens in the United States, candidates must declare their intended university major when they register for the Vestibular. Although it is theoretically possible to switch majors afterwards (in a process known within the universities as <i>transferência interna</i>), that is actually quite rare in Brazil. Undergraduate curricula tend to be more rigid than in the United States and there is little room to take classes outside one's major.
</p><p>Individuals who hold either a bachelor's degree, Licentiate or Technologist are eligible for admission into <a href="/wiki/Graduate_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Graduate School">graduate</a> courses leading to advanced <a href="/wiki/Master%27s_degree" title="Master&#39;s degree">master</a>'s or doctor's degrees. Criteria for admission into master's and doctor's programs vary in Brazil. Some universities require that candidates take entrance exams; others make admission decisions based solely on undergraduate transcripts, letters of recommendation and possibly oral interviews. In most cases, however, especially for the doctorate, the candidate is required to submit a research plan and one faculty member must agree to serve as his/her supervisor before the candidate can be admitted into the program; The exception are the <a href="/wiki/Natural_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural Sciences">Natural Sciences</a> post-graduate programs, that accepts students with very broad and/or vague research prospects with sometimes the prospect is given <i>in promptu</i> during the interview, preferring to let the students define their study program and advisor in the course of the first year of studies.
</p><p>There are two types of post-graduate programs, lato sensu (specialization and MBAs) and stricto sensu (Professional Masters, Master and Doctorate):
</p><p>Specializations or MBAs are courses that include taking a minimum number (minimum 360 hours) of graduate classes but with no need to do research nor defend a thesis, only present a final work showing the knowledge. It's a professional level where theory and practice are focused in a broad sense.
</p><p>Professional Master's or master's degrees usually takes one to two years of full-time study. Requirements for an academic master's degree include taking a minimum number of advanced graduate classes (typically between five and eight)and submitting a research thesis which is examined orally by a panel of at least two examiners (three is the preferred number), sometimes including one external member who must be from another university or research institute. The emphasis of the thesis must be in adding some value to the academic knowledge, but not necessarily in being original.
</p><p>Doctor's degrees normally take four additional years of full-time study to complete. Requirements for obtaining a doctor's degree include taking additional advanced courses, passing an oral qualifying exam and submitting a longer doctoral dissertation which must represent a significant original contribution to knowledge in the field to which the dissertation topic is related. That contrasts with master's thesis, which, in addition to being usually shorter than doctoral dissertations, are not required to include creation of new knowledge or revision/reinterpretation of older views/theories. The doctoral dissertation is examined in a final oral exam before a panel of at least two members (in the state of São Paulo the preferred number is five, while the other regions prefer three members), usually including one or two external examiners from another university or research institute.
</p><p>Finally, a small number of Brazilian universities, most notably the public universities in the state of <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo</a> still award the title of <a href="https://pt.wikipedia.org/wiki/Livre-doc%C3%AAncia" class="extiw" title="pt:Livre-docência">Livre-Docente</a> (<i>free <a href="/wiki/Docent" title="Docent">docent</a></i>), which is of higher standing than a doctorate and is obtained, similar to the German <a href="/wiki/Habilitation" title="Habilitation">Habilitation</a>, by the submission of a second (original or cumulative) thesis and approval in a <i>Livre-Docência</i> examination that includes giving a public lecture before a panel of full professors.
</p><p><i>See also <a href="/wiki/Universities_and_Higher_Education_in_Brazil" class="mw-redirect" title="Universities and Higher Education in Brazil">Universities and Higher Education in Brazil</a></i>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Colombia">Colombia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Colombia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Colombia, the system of academic degrees is based in the British model been similar to the U.S. model. After completing their "bachillerato" (high school), students can take one of three options. The first one is called a "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Profesional</i>" (professional career), which is similar to a bachelor's degree requiring from four to 6 years of study according to the chosen program. The other option is called a "Técnico" (technician); this degree consists in two and a half years of study and prepares the student for technical or mechanical labors. Finally, the third option is called a ¨Tecnólogo¨ (equivalent to associate degree) and consist of 3 years of study.
</p><p>After this, students, now called "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">profesional</i>" (professionals), Tecnólogos (associates) or "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">técnicos</i>" (technicians), can opt for higher degrees.
Formal education after the bachelor's degree is the master's degree with the title of "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Maestro</i>" and Doctorate's degree known as "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Doctorado</i>" (doctorate). The master's degree normally consists of two years.
</p><p>Students also can take an specialization course, "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Especialización</i>", equivalent to a graduate certificate degree, after their bachelor's degree. These programs, like in the U.S. are very popular, because it requires only one to two years of study.
</p><p>A similar situation in Colombia, when compared to the U.S. system, is that the students may not go directly to the "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Doctorado</i>" without having the "Master" degree first.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In Chile, the system in a nutshell is as follows:
Quite similar to the case described for Colombia, students may opt to be "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Profesionales</i>"(Professionals) or "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Técnicos</i>"(Technicians).
After completion of high school, students may follow professional or technical studies at Universities or Technical schools. Only Universities and the Academies of the Armed Forces can give Academic Degrees. In general, traditional professions require an Academic Degree, but there are many professions that not require the degree because they were conceived as strictly "professional" not academic. The degrees are as follows:
</p><p>"<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Licenciado</i>" it is similar to the Bachelor, but to get it is necessary to complete at least eight semesters of study on the subjects which are part of the Major. This degree is enough to continue developing an academic career, however, to get a professional title -which is not academic, but allows you to get a professional practice, you have to continue one or two additional years of study. (For example, to be an engineer it is necessary to study four years to get a Licentiate in Engineering Sciences and two additional years to get a Professional Title and become an engineer. Sometimes it is possible to take additional subjects and get a "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Magister</i>" degree besides the professional title.)
</p><p>"<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Magister</i>" is the equivalent to the master's degree in English speaking countries.
</p><p>"<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Doctorado</i>" is the equivalent to the Doctorate or Phd. There is no separate classification for Professional Doctorates.
</p><p>In particular, the engineering profession may be complicated for the foreigner since there are two types of engineers: those who got an Academic Degree such as Civil Engineers or Armed Forced Politechnical Engineers and those who are "<i lang="es" title="Spanish language text">Ingenieros en Ejecución</i>" (Professional Engineers) which are considered terrain Engineer more focused to apply the engineering in the field and completed only four years of study. They are not able, by law, to authorise plans or drawings like engineers with a degree or architects.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Venezuela">Venezuela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Venezuela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Titles in Venezuela start with the <i>Certificado de Educación Básica</i> (Certificate of Basic Education), awarded upon completing 9th grade. The next title is earned upon completing 11th grade and may be <i>Bachiller en Ciencias</i> (High School Graduate of Science), <i>Bachiller en Humanidades</i> (High School Graduate of Humanities) or <i>Técnico en Ciencias</i> (Science Technician). The reason for this diversity is because some schools provide vocational education as part of their high school curriculum (thereby allowing them to hand out "Technician" titles) while elsewhere, the student is required to decide whether to study Sciences or Humanities for the last two years of secondary school.
</p><p>Titles at the higher education level usually depend on the institution handing them out. Technical schools award the student with the title of <i>Técnico Superior Universitario</i> (University Higher Technician, to distinguish from Science Technician). Universities award the student with the title of <i>Ingeniero</i> (Engineer) or with the title <i>Licenciado</i> (Licentiate) after completing a five-year program. The Engineer have more physics subjects than the Licentiate, but both are five-year careers. Some higher education institutions may award <i>Diplomados</i> (Diploma) but the time necessary to obtain one varies. Medical Doctors are awarded the title "Médico Cirujano" after completing a 6 year-career.
</p><p>Post-graduate education follows conventions of the United States (being named "Master's" and "Doctorate" after the programs there)
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pontifical_universities">Pontifical universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Academic_degree&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Pontifical universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Pontifical_university" title="Pontifical university">Pontifical universities</a> around the world such as the Pontifical University, St Patrick's College, Maynooth in Ireland, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Santo_Tomas" title="University of Santo Tomas">Pontifical and Royal University of Santo Tomas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">Manila</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Catholic_University_of_America" class="mw-redirect" title="The Catholic University of America">The Catholic University of America</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_University_of_Saint_Thomas_Aquinas" title="Pontifical University of Saint Thomas Aquinas">Pontifical University of Saint Thomas Aquinas</a>, <i>Angelicum</i> in Rome, the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_catholique_de_Louvain" title="Université catholique de Louvain">University of Louvain</a> (UCLouvain) in Belgium and the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Peru" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Peru">Pontifical Catholic University of Peru</a> depend for their status as pontifical universities and for the nature of their academic degrees on the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_Catholic_Education" title="Congregation for Catholic Education">Congregation for Catholic Education</a>.  The nature of academic degrees from ecclesiastical institutions of education is outlined in the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_constitution" title="Apostolic constitution">apostolic constitution</a> <i>Sapientia Christiana</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-vatican.va_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vatican.va-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In distinction to secular or Catholic universities, which are academic institutions for the study and teaching of a broad range of disciplines, Ecclesiastical or <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_university" title="Pontifical university">Pontifical universities</a> "are usually composed of three principal ecclesiastical faculties, theology, philosophy and canon law and at least one other faculty.  A Pontifical university specifically addresses Christian revelation and disciplines correlative to the evangelical mission of the Church as set out in the apostolic constitution <i>Sapientia christiana</i>."<sup id="cite_ref-vatican.va_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vatican.va-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-avepro.va_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-avepro.va-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are three cycles of degrees that constitute the core of degrees granted by pontifical universities: the first cycle leading to the <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor&#39;s degree">baccalaureate</a> degree; the second cycle leading to the <a href="/wiki/Licentiate_(degree)" title="Licentiate (degree)">licentiate</a> degree; the third cycle leading to the <a href="/wiki/Doctorate" title="Doctorate">doctorate</a>.  From this core pontifical universities confer degrees including:<br />Theology:
</p>
<ul><li>Baccalaureate in Sacred Theology, <i>Sacrae Theologiae Baccalaureatus</i> (S.T.B.)</li>
<li>Licentiate in Sacred Theology, <i>Sacrae Theologiae Licentiatus</i> (S.T.L.)</li>
<li>Doctorate in Sacred Theology, <i>Sacrae Theologiae Doctoratus</i> (S.T.D.)</li></ul>
<p>Philosophy:
</p>
<ul><li>Baccalaureate in Philosophy, <i>Philosophiae Baccalaureatus</i> (Ph.B.)</li>
<li>Licentiate in Philosophy, <i>Philosophiae Licentiatus</i> (Ph.L.)</li>
<li>Doctorate in Philosophy, <i>Philosophiae Doctoratus</i> (Ph.D.)</li></ul>
<p>Canon Law:
</p>
<ul><li>Baccalaureate in Canon Law, <i>Juris Canonici Baccalaureatus</i> (J.C.B.)</li>
<li>Licentiate in Canon Law, <i>Iuris Canonici Licentiatus</i> (J.C.L.)</li>
<li>Doctorate in Canon Law, <i>Iuris Canonici Doctoratus</i> (J.C.D.)</li></ul>

<li id="cite_note-Makdisi-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Makdisi_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite id="CITEREFMakdisi1989" class="citation"><a href="/wiki/George_Makdisi" title="George Makdisi">Makdisi, George</a> (April–June 1989), "Scholasticism and Humanism in Classical Islam and the Christian West", <i>Journal of the American Oriental Society</i>, <b>109</b> (2): 175–182 [175–77], <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.2307%2F604423">10.2307/604423</a>, <a href="/wiki/JSTOR" title="JSTOR">JSTOR</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.jstor.org/stable/604423">604423</a></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+the+American+Oriental+Society&amp;rft.atitle=Scholasticism+and+Humanism+in+Classical+Islam+and+the+Christian+West&amp;rft.volume=109&amp;rft.issue=2&amp;rft.pages=175-182+175-77&amp;rft.date=1989-04%2F1989-06&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.2307%2F604423&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fwww.jstor.org%2Fstable%2F604423&amp;rft.aulast=Makdisi&amp;rft.aufirst=George&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAcademic+degree" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>

<li id="cite_note-Alatas-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Alatas_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Alatas_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal"><a href="/wiki/Syed_Farid_al-Attas" title="Syed Farid al-Attas">Al-Attas, Syed Farid</a> (1 January 2006). "From Jāmi' ah to University: Multiculturalism and Christian–Muslim Dialogue". <i><a href="/wiki/Current_Sociology" title="Current Sociology">Current Sociology</a></i>. <b>54</b> (1): 112–132. <a href="/wiki/Digital_object_identifier" title="Digital object identifier">doi</a>:<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//doi.org/10.1177%2F0011392106058837">10.1177/0011392106058837</a>. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">ISSN</a>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/issn/0011-3921">0011-3921</a>. <q>In the 1930s, the renowned Orientalist Alfred Guillaume noted strong resemblances between Muslim and Western Christian institutions of higher learning. An example he cited is the ijazah, which he recognized as being akin to the medieval licentia docendi, the precursor of the modern university degree.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Current+Sociology&amp;rft.atitle=From+J%C4%81mi%27+ah+to+University%3A+Multiculturalism+and+Christian%E2%80%93Muslim+Dialogue&amp;rft.volume=54&amp;rft.issue=1&amp;rft.pages=112-132&amp;rft.date=2006-01-01&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1177%2F0011392106058837&amp;rft.issn=0011-3921&amp;rft.aulast=Al-Attas&amp;rft.aufirst=Syed+Farid&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAcademic+degree" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-stewart-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-stewart_7-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia"><a href="/wiki/Devin_J._Stewart" title="Devin J. Stewart">Devin J. Stewart</a> (2005). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=c1ZsBgAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA201">"Degrees, or Ijazah"</a>.  In Josef W. Meri (ed.). <i><a href="/wiki/Medieval_Islamic_Civilization:_An_Encyclopedia" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval Islamic Civilization: An Encyclopedia">Medieval Islamic Civilization: An Encyclopedia</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Routledge" title="Routledge">Routledge</a>. pp.&#160;201–203. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781135455965" title="Special:BookSources/9781135455965"><bdi>9781135455965</bdi></a>. <q>The license to teach law and issue legal opinions [...] is the type of ijazah that resembles the medieval European university degree most closely [...] The main difference between the two is that the granting authority is an individual professor, in the Islamic case, rather than a corporate institution in the case of the university. Despite this point, Makdisi has likened the ijazat al-ifta’ wa’l-tadris to the medieval Latin licentia docendi and suggests that it served as a model for that degree.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Degrees%2C+or+Ijazah&amp;rft.btitle=Medieval+Islamic+Civilization%3A+An+Encyclopedia&amp;rft.pages=201-203&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.isbn=9781135455965&amp;rft.au=Devin+J.+Stewart&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dc1ZsBgAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA201&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAcademic+degree" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/></span>
